The National Central University Student National Salvation Association Hosted the Press Yesterday, Beiping Student Representatives Reported Everything 18

Nanjing: The Student National Salvation Association of National Central University hosted the press in the afternoon of the 22nd, stating the motives and attitudes of the school's students in deciding on the national salvation movement, as well as the future direction, and hoped that the media would provide more assistance. In addition, all the students of National Central University telegraphed the students of various schools in Beiping to express condolences and issued a declaration, requesting consistent voices. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing: For the patriotic movement of students in Beiping, all the students of National Central University hosted reporters from Beijing at the library at 3:00 PM on the afternoon of the 22nd. More than 30 people attended. First, the students of National Central University reported on the motives, attitudes, and details of the patriotic movement, hoping that the media would give fair reports and accurate criticisms of the student patriotic movement. Finally, it was declared that there were no arrests, disappearances, or strikes among the students of National Central University. Then, two student representatives who came to Beijing from Beiping on the morning of the 22nd were introduced to report on the process of the student petition parade and the truth of the incident in Beiping, saying that the students and the military police clashed as reported, but the students had no weapons, how could they resist? They only tasted the taste of being beaten by whips, broadswords, and bayonets. More than 300 people were injured in the parade on the 16th, and 21 people were missing. Tears welled up when they spoke. Tea and refreshments were served at 5:00 PM. (22nd Dispatch)

Troops from the 32nd Army Are Stationed South of Shunde 19

Tianjin: The divisions and teams of the 32nd Army of Shang Zhen have all concentrated on the south of Shunde on foot by the 22nd. The teams in Cangxian and Jinghai were completed and left on the 21st. (22nd Dispatch)

President Jiang Rectifies Office Hours 20

Nanjing: President Jiang, because the office hours of various affiliated agencies are uneven, and some are less than eight hours a day, has ordered a rectification. In addition to the Ministry of Education, which has complied, various ministries will be extended from next week. (22nd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Recent Developments in Customs Revenue 21

Nanjing: According to the Customs Administration, customs revenue in the past year has been affected by the decline in the world economy, the lack of recovery in domestic rural areas, the decline in industry and commerce, and the lack of trade. On the one hand, the promotion of domestic goods has reduced the import of foreign goods. The Ministry of Finance estimates that the customs revenue for the 23rd year will increase by 12 million yuan compared with the actual revenue in the 22nd year. Among them, both import and export taxes have increased, while transshipment taxes have decreased slightly. The reason is that the import tariff implemented in July of the 23rd year aims to protect the domestic product tax rate. There are more increases and fewer decreases. Therefore, import taxes have still increased. As for the new export tax rate implemented in June of the 23rd year, most of them have been reduced compared to before, but tax revenue has still increased slightly. The decrease in transshipment tax is mainly due to the abolition of the transshipment tax on postal packages and the exemption of industrial products. However, since the beginning of this year, the import of goods from outside Shanhaiguan has been less, and domestic purchases are weak. In addition, the special circumstances in North China have greatly reduced import tariffs. (22nd Dispatch)

Current Affairs Commentary

New Trends in Anglo-American Relations 22

— Star

Since the North China issue has become serious and the naval conference has opened, relations between Britain and the United States have shown a new trend. On the 5th of this month, the British Foreign Secretary and the US Secretary of State issued statements at the same time, one expressing concern about the North China issue and recognizing that interference in China's internal affairs is unfortunate, and the other expressing that the powers have a collective obligation on the China issue and must strictly abide by the Nine-Power Treaty. At the naval conference, Britain showed concessions on its long-standing advocacy of medium-sized warships and accepted the US's large-sized principle, willing to limit the maximum tonnage to 32,000 tons. This issue was the center of the dispute between Britain and the United States on naval issues. Britain's willingness to concede must have its own intentions. Recently, a member of the British House of Lords even suggested that Britain and the United States conclude a naval defense treaty. Although this proposal is idealistic, it can also be seen that this is the general trend of British opinion.

According to this ideal, Britain should open its important naval ports, such as Singapore, to the United States so that the US fleet can use British military ports. The United States should also open US military ports, docks, and fuel stations to Britain. In this way, any country can be prevented from carrying out aggression in the ocean. The basis of this ideal is the recent agreement signed by Britain and France, that is, France allows British ships to use French military ports when the British fleet is attacked. If this proposal is applied to a corner of the Far East, it may be possible to realize it. If it is generally applicable, it is not allowed by the facts. In the Far East, the interests of Britain and the United States are consistent. Britain lacks a fleet, while the United States lacks military ports. It is said that once the United States is in trouble in the Far East, if Britain does not allow it to borrow Hong Kong, the power of the US fleet will be greatly reduced. The mutual opening of naval ports is to enhance the power to deter aggression and to properly guard the western coast of the Pacific.

Although the extent to which Anglo-American cooperation has materialized is unknown to us, there are still many political issues to be resolved before negotiating this kind of military cooperation method. The situation in the Far East has reached the point where Britain has no ability to resist Japan alone and has no possibility of compromising with Japan. The only way is to ally with the United States to defend itself. It is very obvious that the United States wants to maintain its open-door policy and keep the Philippine Islands safe, and it also needs the help of Britain. However, the United States is a democratic country, and the president has no power to sign secret treaties, and the president's promises are often rejected by Congress. It is really difficult for Britain to rely on the United States for help. The guarantee of the State Council is not completely reliable. Moreover, the current Neutrality Act still prevents the president from signing a military alliance with any country. This is an obstacle on the American side. Britain has always adopted pragmatism in the Far East, and allying with Japan and the United States is always based on convenience. Simon's failure to accept Stimson's proposal after the September 18th Incident has made those in the United States who advocate cooperation feel chilled. If this attitude does not change, the United States will not be willing to cooperate. This is the gap on the British side. Although Britain and the United States have reached a point in the Far East where they will both lose if they are divided and both benefit if they are united, it is believed that the politicians of the two countries will be able to work hard to break this obstacle and actively cooperate.

Nanjing. The Ministry of Finance is reorganizing salt production to increase transportation and sales, unify the tax system, and strictly enforce anti-smuggling measures. Currently, the existing salt warehouses along the Xiang, Hubei, West Anhui banks are insufficient. After careful consideration of the riverbank situation, it has been decided to build main warehouses. The site for the Xiang bank warehouse, capable of holding forty batches of salt, has been surveyed and determined in Yueyang. The site for the West bank warehouse has also been surveyed and determined in Jiujiang. A suitable site has been found in Wuhu Datong for the Anhui bank warehouse, in preparation for construction, to establish a foundation for tax collection at the salt production site. (22nd Dispatch)

Says War is a Foolish Act and Contrary to Humanity; Does Not Intend to Protest Pittman's Remarks

After the Naval Conference Adjourns: US and Japan Hold Brief Talks 71

Security and Armaments Equality: Difficult Compromise as Britain, US, and Japan Argue

London: Following the adjournment of the Naval Conference, Norman Davis, the chief representative of the United States, and Admiral Standley, the Chief of Naval Operations, visited the Japanese representatives at Grosvenor House at 5:30 PM today. The talks lasted only half an hour and did not involve lengthy discussions about the future development of the Naval Conference. Davis is scheduled to travel to Switzerland with Mrs. Philips, the Under Secretary of State, on Monday to spend Christmas and will return here in early January to participate in the Naval Conference. (Havas News Agency, 21st)

London: The Japanese delegation released a statement on the 21st regarding the progress of the disarmament conference to date and Japan's position, stating: "The conference is proceeding as initially planned, and there have been ample opportunities to explain Japan's position. We are very satisfied that the common upper limit has been fully explored. Generally speaking, Japan's position is based on three points: 1. Establishing equal rights in armaments; 2. Ensuring that the common upper limit is set at the lowest possible level to achieve actual disarmament; 3. Abolishing or drastically reducing offensive weapons and establishing the principle of making defense easy and offense difficult, thereby avoiding threats and aggression. To date, the relationship between security equality and armaments equality has been the subject of debate. Although Britain has raised the issue of vulnerability, naval forces are highly mobile and can concentrate forces quickly. The voyage of the Baltic Fleet to the Far East and other examples are numerous. Tactically, a force of three cannot compete with a force of five. Determining quality without determining quantity benefits the UK and US, which have large quantities, but is extremely unfavorable to Japan. The British proposal only discusses principles and is not fully clear. However, its key point is that the military strength required by each country varies depending on the size of its responsibilities, which is fundamentally different from Japan's position. Therefore, Japan has reiterated that it must return to the Japanese proposal. However, a final rejection of the British proposal has not yet been expressed, but Britain should also understand that it is difficult for Japan to accept." (Dentsu News Agency, 22nd)

London: The Standard Evening News recently commented on Japan's demand for a common upper limit on naval forces, saying, "If this demand is realized, Japan's position in the western Pacific will inevitably become impregnable. If disputes arise with Britain and the United States in that region in the future, they will have to defer to Japan. Japan has vital interests in the Western Pacific, just as we do in the English Channel and the North Sea. This is undeniable. However, due to the constraints of current treaties, Britain and the United States cannot establish naval bases near the Japanese islands in the Pacific. Even if the naval ratio remains the same, Japan's naval power is already more than sufficient to resist attacks. How can it be granted equal rights? This so-called naval equality for Japan is not based on security concerns but is actually necessary for the country's prestige. All demands based on national prestige lead to mutual suspicion and jealousy, creating a general sense of insecurity, and the danger of war breaking out is also worrisome. Therefore, the Naval Conference should focus on the mutual security of all countries concerned, which would be beneficial in practice." (Havas News Agency, 21st)

London: The Spectator Weekly recently commented on the Naval Conference, saying, "If the 'quantitative restriction' proposal put forward by Naval Minister Lord Monsell on behalf of the British government yesterday can be implemented, the unrestricted naval competition among countries can at least be prevented in the near future, and there can be a slight respite. Even if various agreements are unlikely to be reached at present, it is still possible to sign them in the future. As for the idea that each naval power should notify each other of future shipbuilding programs, the United States still believes that the original rationale has not been fully exhausted and that separate provisions can be formally agreed upon. However, this program may be slightly modified within certain limits. If the Naval Conference can achieve this, and limit the tonnage and gun caliber of various warships, it would be a truly worthwhile endeavor." (Havas News Agency, 21st)

The purpose of Japan's protests was to prevent the silver in North China from being extracted by the central government. Establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council 84

Xiao and Qin Visit Doihara to Exchange Views: The Nature of the Chahar Issue is Extremely Serious

Northern Communication, the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council was announced on the 18th. In addition to Zhou Zuomin in Shanghai, Wang Kemin, Cheng Ke sick, and Jia Deyao who did not take office, a total of 13 people attended the inauguration ceremony. The time of the grand ceremony was 8:00 am, and the notification was received late on the 17th, so only more than 80 people attended the ceremony. Security was extremely tight inside and outside the Foreign Affairs Building, and special personnel were responsible for taking care of the guests and Chinese and foreign journalists, in order to prevent radical elements from taking any action. The Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Council was originally scheduled to be established on the 16th, but was temporarily shelved due to circumstances. It was then contacted on the evening of the 17th, and it was decided to establish it on the 18th. Because the Japanese side has never abandoned its original position, there are two reasons why it was finally able to concede: 1. During the Naval Disarmament Conference, the Japanese side was fully engaged in dealing with the conference, so it temporarily relaxed its grip on North China. 2. The overall adjustment of Sino-Japanese relations has already begun. Japanese soldiers close to the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs are holding strong opinions. After the establishment of the council, the most important task at hand is how to deal with the "Hebei East" and "Chahar North" issues, which is also the touchstone of the council's credibility with the people of the country. Therefore, after the completion of the inauguration ceremony, Chairman Song Zheyuan immediately sent Xiao Zhenying and Qin Dechun to the Fusan Hall to meet with Doihara Kenji, the head of the Japanese Kwantung Army's special agency, to discuss the matter. At that time, because the Chahar North issue was close to being resolved, only the solution of the Hebei East issue was discussed, and a long conversation of two hours was held. Xiao and Qin then returned to Wu Yiku Hutong to visit Song and report. Xiao Zhenying also decided to go to Tianjin on the morning of the 19th to take up the post of mayor of Tianjin.

The future disposition of the "Hebei East" puppet organization, according to indirect sources, is divided into three steps: 1. Yin Rugeng voluntarily abolishes the puppet organization. 2. The authorities here will speak to the government on behalf of Yin to ask for leniency. 3. Handle the aftermath. As far as the current situation is concerned, these three items can only be described as a proposal on our side. The Japanese side's expression, as of now, is only within the four words "can be considered". Therefore, the authorities here are prepared to continue contact in the short term, but it is heard that Doihara has left Ping for Tianjin today (20th) and will return to Shenyang within a few days. The military attache of the Japanese Embassy in Peiping, Imai, only arrived in Ping today (20th) to take over. When will the talks be resumed? It will be necessary to consult the Japanese side's opinion in advance before a decision can be made.

Regarding the organization of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, the outline has not yet been announced, but it is credible that in addition to the committee electing three standing committee members to be responsible for handling daily affairs, there will be three departments: Secretariat, Political Affairs, and Finance, which will carry out council affairs under the orders of the standing committee. When necessary, a number of specialized committees may be established. It is heard that in the near future, there will be three specialized committees: Foreign Affairs, Transportation, and Culture. These committees are research and design agencies, so they will recruit various specialized technicians to take on the responsibilities. As for the candidates for the heads of the three departments: Secretariat, Political Affairs, and Finance, the council decided at its second meeting this morning (20th) to appoint Ge Dingyuan as acting head of the Secretariat, Pan Yugui as acting head of the Political Affairs Department, and Guo Zhihan as acting head of the Finance Department, pending a clear order from the central government before they are formally appointed. The council has already sent a telegram to the central government recommending them.

Regarding the "Chahar North" issue, its seriousness is even greater than the so-called "autonomy movement". Therefore, the authorities' response has been quite painstaking. It is said that the Japanese side demands that the six counties of Guyuan, Bingchang, Kangbao, Zhangbei, Huade, and Shangdu be garrisoned by the Mongolian security forces, and that the administrative power of the six counties be ceded together. The reason is said to be the necessary action to complete its Manchuria-Mongolia policy. The authorities ordered the security forces defending the city to swear to coexist with the city and not to abandon it lightly, while negotiating with the Japanese side, arguing based on reason. Finally, our side expressed that in any case, both sides would make concessions at the same time. During the negotiations, Zhangjiakou frequently telegraphed information about the stalemate on the front line. Until the previous day (18th), it was proven that there was no more war on the front line, and the news also subsided. According to the Japanese side, the Mongolian security forces are organized by the Mongolian Political Affairs Council and led by Zhuo Shihai. The authorities therefore summoned Bao Yueqing, the resident representative of the Mongolian Political Affairs Council in Ping, to inquire about the truth. Bao said that he had not received any telegram from the Mongolian Council regarding this matter, so he could not answer. In order to clarify the truth and avoid misunderstandings among the people, Bao agreed to go to Pangjiang to meet with Prince De. The authorities were very pleased, so Bao left Beiping a few days ago. Tonight (20th), the relevant parties here received a telegram from Bao reporting that he had arrived in Pangjiang. The process of visiting Prince De was not mentioned, only that he would come to Ping in a few days. It is generally speculated that the truth about Chahar North will be clear after Bao arrives in Ping. (December 20th)

Yin Ju-keng Tries Hard to Expand the Pseudo-Eastern Hebei Region 85

Extending Occupation to Areas Around Xinhe and Tanggu / Customs and Salt Taxes Have Not Yet Been Intercepted

Tianjin dispatch: Since the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, the issue of the pseudo-Eastern Hebei organization has not yet been resolved. Tanggu, Xinhe, Changping, and Ninghe have all been forcibly occupied by security teams dispatched by the pseudo-organization, who drove out officials of the provincial government. Furthermore, a pseudo-Eastern Hebei Bank was established in Tongzhou to issue banknotes. Judging from these events, the pseudo-Eastern Hebei organization seems determined to maintain its separatist power, making it extremely difficult to seek compromise or its voluntary abolition.

In the defense area of the 32nd Army at Tanghe, the Zhao Lei unit of the 4th Security Brigade of Eastern Hebei arrived within the past week and demanded the handover of barracks, leading to a brief conflict. After a battalion of the 961st Regiment of the 29th Army arrived, the 32nd Army relinquished the barracks, including the Xinhe railway station defense area. On the 18th, the 32nd Army began to concentrate from Bunan towards Shunde and Baoding. As the 29th Army was deploying to Tanggu and Xinhe, with the 653rd Regiment headquarters planning to proceed to Lutai and Ninghe for takeover, Yin Ju-keng again ordered Zhao Lei's unit to maintain vigilance and dig trenches in those two areas, preventing their advance.

Yin, accompanied by his Japanese advisor Ninomiya, secretly came to Tianjin by car and met with the new Chief of Staff of the Japanese Garrison in Tianjin, Toshiyasu Nagami; the Chief of the China Section of the Japanese Army General Staff, Seiichi Kita; and the Head of the Japanese Special Service Agency in Shanhaiguan, Takeashita Yukiharu. He requested them to negotiate with Song Zheyuan to prevent the 29th Army troops from crossing Junliangcheng. The original defense areas of the 32nd Army in Ninghe, Lutai, Xinhe, and Tanggu were to be handed over to the security teams under the pseudo-organization's rule. Nagami then went to Peiping on the 18th to visit Song Zheyuan regarding this matter.

By the evening of the same day, the troops of the 29th Army that had already arrived in Xinhe and Tanggu were ordered to retreat to Junliangcheng for garrison. Not a single soldier of the regular army remained east of Tanggu. The various agencies in Ninghe had long been forcibly occupied by the pseudo-organization, which also appointed Zhu Yi, the former magistrate of Leting County, as the new magistrate. In Tanggu, the central and provincial government agencies were guarded by security teams, and official documents and funds were forced to be submitted to the Tangshan Anti-Communist Autonomous Committee of Eastern Hebei. Wu Longfu, the Director of the Tanggu Public Security Bureau, was expelled and replaced by Zhu Bo, the deputy commander of the 4th Security Brigade, dispatched by the pseudo-organization.

Currently, the pseudo-region of Yin Ju-keng is gradually expanding, already approaching Tianjin. Tanggu is less than 50 li from Tianjin. If the Hebei-Chahar Political Council is unable to abolish the pseudo-Eastern Hebei organization, Tianjin may also be engulfed, which is a matter of serious concern.

After the pseudo-Eastern Hebei organization intercepted the customs and salt taxes of eastern Luanhe, although the customs duties were not allowed to be remitted to the central government and were temporarily kept by the collecting agencies, in reality, the customs offices did not comply. The pseudo-organization, lacking a proper plan, did not resort to coercive interference. As for the salt taxes, the Changlu Salt Tax Inspection Office has two salt marshes under its jurisdiction, both located within the current pseudo-region: the Lutai marsh and the Fengcai marsh. The Lutai marsh is located on the coast of Lutai Town, while the Fengcai marsh is located in the Tanggu and Hangu area.

Last year, the two marshes collected over 20 million yuan in salt taxes. This year's performance is even better, with over 25 million yuan already collected. In the past, salt taxes were collected and paid by the marshes and agencies to the Tianjin Inspection Office and deposited in the Central Bank. The annual revenue, after repaying foreign debts secured by salt taxes and the interest on the post-Boxer Protocol loan of 1913, was used to subsidize military expenses in North China. Since 1934, due to war zone public debt collateral, an additional 1.5 million yuan has been spent annually.

The Ministry of Finance believes that there is no need for excessive concern regarding the pseudo-Eastern Hebei organization's interception of customs and salt taxes, as the customs duty interception is difficult to achieve, and there is no salt tax to deduct. If the two marshes are controlled and salt production for external sales is prevented, Lu salt and Huai salt can be transported within the Changlu salt sales area as substitutes. The war zone public debt interest of 1.5 million yuan can be suspended. If Yin relies solely on the revenue from the 22 counties to sustain itself, it may be difficult to maintain for long. (20th)

Peiping / Schools Have Not Yet Resumed Classes 86

Six University Presidents Send Another Letter to Students Urging Resumption / Song Zheyuan Asks University Presidents to Strictly Manage Students

Peiping dispatch: The patriotic student movement in Peiping has slightly eased today (20th) after persuasion from various parties, but internal activities are still quite active. Here are the situations from various aspects:

Professors from Various Universities Visit Qin

Li Jianxun of Normal University, Yan Shutang of the College of Law and Commerce, and Zhu Jie of the China College visited Mayor Qin Dechun at 10 AM today (20th). After the professors explained their intentions, Qin immediately stated that student strikes and petitions are indeed patriotic movements but are detrimental to public order and should not be expanded. He asked the professors to persuade them, and so on.

Jiang Menglin Elaborates on Solutions

The reporter interviewed Jiang Menglin, the president of Peking University, today (20th). According to his remarks: "This student patriotic movement is inherently pure. Students view petitions and marches as a way to arouse public patriotism. Local authorities feel the difficulty of maintaining order. We are willing to peacefully persuade the students to stop off-campus activities as soon as possible. The president's authority can use a peaceful attitude to guide the students to the best of his ability and will never use stricter methods to forcibly stop their actions. The president can give sincere advice to students based on the telegram from the Ministry of Education. If students have opinions on political current events, they can submit them in writing to the president, who will then forward them to the government. However, the president cannot expel students because of their patriotism; I think all parties can understand this. Since the student petition on the 9th, the presidents of the universities have jointly issued a letter to the students, advising them to resume their studies immediately. Today, a second announcement to the students was issued, still advising the students to resume classes immediately, which shows that the presidents have always been responsible for persuading the students."

Students Temporarily Do Not Demonstrate

According to sources on the student side, students from various schools in Peiping will not be passive because of the arrest of students by the military police, nor will they be afraid because of student injuries or deaths. They are now uniting internally, closely contacting students in various provinces and cities, and working together for a unified patriotic movement. They will temporarily not march or demonstrate in the recent few days and will not make sacrifices without any return. However, it does not mean that they will not sacrifice again; they will show their determination when the time is ripe. The authorities of various schools have tried hard to persuade them, and the students are not unreasonable, but this is a patriotic movement of the entire student community, which cannot be answered by one or two individuals or schools. Currently, all national and private universities in Peiping have gone on strike, and municipal and private middle schools have followed suit. The resumption of classes cannot be discussed at this moment. As long as the local authorities restrain the police, do not make things difficult for the students, and, even more so, do not make things difficult for the female students, the student movement can be eased.

Six University Presidents Send Another Letter to Students

The presidents of the six universities in Peiping issued a second letter to the students today (20th), which reads: "Dear students, after the student petition march of Peiping schools on December 9th, we jointly issued a letter to the students, pointing out that "the goals of your petitions and strikes can be said to have been achieved. We hope that you will not create complications, waste time, and resume your studies immediately." Unexpectedly, after that letter was issued, there was a large-scale student march in Peiping on the 16th, with thousands of participants and nearly a hundred injured. We, of course, sympathize with the expression of patriotic sentiments of the young students. However, such mass action has the function of protest, but it is not a practical method of saving the country. You are all in the learning stage. Two protests are enough to awaken the public and inform the world. The actual matter of serving the country definitely cannot be effective with bare hands, shouting slogans, and distributing flyers. Young students, after identifying the goal of serving the country, should strive to train themselves to become knowledgeable and capable talents to meet the needs of the country. If you waste your studies and time, not only will it be of no benefit to serving and saving the country, but it is simply young people abandoning their own responsibilities and destroying the future pillars of the country. Now all the arrested students have been released on bail, and the injured students are gradually recovering. We sincerely hope that you will resume classes immediately. The matter of serving the country is a heavy responsibility and a long road. Young people must not be misled by a momentary impulse and neglect the preparation for serving the country in the future. Jiang Menglin, President of Peking University; Xu Songming, Acting President of Peiping University; Mei Yi-qi, President of Tsinghua University; Li Zheng, President of Normal University; Wang Zhuoran, Acting President of Northeastern University; Lu Zhiwei, Acting President of Yenching University."

Song Zheyuan Writes to University Presidents

Song Zheyuan issued a letter to the presidents of the universities, which reads: "Recently, students from various schools in the city have been confused by rumors, leading to marches and strikes. Despite repeated persuasion and sanctions, classes have not been resumed. If this continues, not only will time be wasted, but it will also affect the local area. As I am responsible for security, how dare I sit idly by? I have previously informed the students of the schools in writing, but there are still things I cannot help but say. The future rise and fall of the nation depend entirely on the young students. The ability of the students to achieve success today depends entirely on the teachers of the schools. Because when students leave home to enter school, it is no different from entrusting their lives to the teachers in the school. On ordinary days, they use rewards and punishments to help them become talents. In an emergency, they should take on hard work and complaints to correct their mistakes. Today's student thinking cannot be guided by the government's painful explanations. Still, using administrative power to suppress and deter not only causes misunderstandings of destroying education but also raises suspicions of stepping into the shoes of others. Because the responsibility and authority for managing students all lie with the president. Even if stricter methods are used to force their actions, they should also be handled by the president according to the academy's regulations. Moreover, the number of students is large, and their qualities are uneven. Some even distribute communist leaflets. Such actions, if in normal times, the teachers in the school would seem to be inappropriate to let go, let alone at this time when the country is in difficulty. I do not mean to say that the presidents do not bear responsibility for the actions of these students. However, in today's situation, things are very difficult. Only by being in the same boat can we help each other. All sectors of politics and academia exchange opinions and are not afraid of details. I humbly take the meaning of the "Spring and Autumn Annals" to prepare for the worthy, and I sincerely hope that the teachers of the schools, together with the government, will take on the hard work and complaints and overcome the difficulties together. Each should adopt strict sanctions and effective methods based on the situation of their own school in order to return to normal as soon as possible, so that I can also fulfill my private desire to value the young people and protect the school. I am very fortunate, very fortunate. Song Zheyuan" (20th)

Popular Science Series / Edited by the Chinese Science Society

Talking About Rabies (Also Known as Madness in Dogs) 88

— Luo Qingsheng

Rabies has a history of two thousand years in our country. There are records of the people chasing rabid dogs in the seventeenth year of Duke Zhao of Lu (566 B.C.). The so-called rabid dogs are the mad dogs of today.

This disease is widespread in our country, occurring in almost every place. Areas where stray dogs gather are even more of a medium for spreading this disease. After a dog becomes infected, if it bites someone and they are not treated quickly, their life is at risk. In addition to humans, other domestic animals such as pigs, horses, cattle, sheep, cats, and even poultry can be infected.

The pathogen of rabies has not yet been isolated and cultured. Even the Negri bodies, which are recognized by most scholars as the pathogen, cannot be definitively identified. The incubation period of the disease varies, with the average shown in the following table:

If the wound is deep, there are many viruses, the virulence is strong, and the distance to the central nervous system is short, then the incubation period is shorter; otherwise, it is longer. Only 20% to 30% of domestic animals that are bitten by rabid dogs develop the disease.

Ninety percent of human rabies cases are transmitted by rabid dogs, and the rest are transmitted by cats, wolves, and other livestock. The mortality rate of people bitten by rabid dogs is 16% to 20%. According to Babes, the mortality rate from being bitten by rabid wolves is 60% to 90%.

Dogs are an important medium for transmitting this disease, and dogs have been companions to humans for thousands of years. Today, in large cities and remote villages, dogs and humans live together. If there is no clear understanding of this disease, the danger is especially great. Therefore, the symptoms of rabies are described in detail below:

Prodromal Stage: The sick dog is depressed, easily irritated, likes to hide in dark places, and does not like to be approached by people. It may also be affectionate to acquaintances but bite at strangers. Its appetite changes, and it craves indigestible substances such as dirt, dry grass, wood chips, and gravel. The wound is strangely itchy, and it often licks it with its tongue or gnaws at it with its teeth. Sometimes it behaves as usual. Excretion of feces and urine is often difficult.

Excitation Stage: The sick dog is restless, and its temperament suddenly becomes ferocious. It aimlessly attacks animals, chairs, tables, spittoons, etc. It likes to roam far from home and does not show any signs of fatigue. When it encounters other dogs, cattle, horses, sheep, or pigs, it fights fiercely without making a sound. It often fears people, but when stimulated or threatened, it also attacks them. During this period, there are often symptoms of nerve paralysis. The most important symptom is the change in sound, which is rough, loud, and long, different from that of a normal dog. Experienced people can tell that it is infected with rabies simply by hearing it. In addition, appetite disappears, and even drinking water is difficult.

Paralytic Stage: During this period, the paralytic state is more obvious. The mouth is often open, the tongue is hanging down, saliva is flowing out of the mouth, the upper eyelid is drooping, there is strabismus, the cornea is dark and dull, and the pupils are dilated. Paralysis of the limbs is first discovered in the hind legs, and walking is unstable. Soon, the rear part is completely paralyzed and lies on the ground. Paralysis progresses rapidly to the front part of the body. At this time, the sick dog is extremely emaciated and exhausted, and it soon dies. Before death, there are often convulsions. When cats are infected with this disease, their symptoms are the same as those of dogs.

The course of the disease is usually four to seven days, but it can be as short as three days or as long as two or three weeks. Rabies is an incurable disease, and self-healing is extremely rare. After a rabid dog bites someone, it is advisable to try to capture or kill the dog (but do not completely destroy the brain, because the hippocampus of the brain is often used to examine for Negri bodies) and send it to a hospital or health agency for examination to determine whether it has rabies. If the diagnosis is confirmed, the bitten person should undergo Pasteur's treatment. If there is no treatment equipment, the wound should be bled profusely and washed with disinfectant water, such as pure alcohol, 3% carbolic acid, or 1% mercuric chloride, to eliminate the virus. In short, the earlier the treatment after being bitten by a rabid dog, the more hope there is. After a few hours or a few days, there is no certainty. Once symptoms appear, it is too late to save the person. As for the miraculous or secret formulas for treating rabies that are occasionally published in newspapers, after reading them carefully, they are laughable. They do not conform to scientific principles and have no experimental proof, misleading people.

Nowadays, foreign cities are extremely cautious in preventing rabies and have strict regulations to crack down on stray dogs and dog owners. In contrast, in the urban areas of our country, stray dogs are everywhere, and there are frequent reports of rabid dogs biting people. Although there are no accurate statistics on the loss of life, given the large population and the large number of stray dogs, the number is probably not small.

Rabies preventive vaccines have been studied by scholars in various countries for decades and have achieved considerable results. The Central Epidemic Prevention Office in Peiping, our country, also manufactures rabies vaccines. Each 7cc dose costs 2 yuan and is enough to inject one dog. The immunity period is one year.

On the 20th, they held a march and demonstration. However, students in Wuchang were unable to cross the river to Hankou for the march because the ferry service was suspended on that day. Feeling dissatisfied, a portion of the students camped out overnight under the Yellow Crane Tower at the Hanyangmen Wharf. Another portion of students stood vigil in front of the Provincial Government, petitioning overnight. By 2:00 AM on the 21st, students gathered in increasing numbers along Pingyue Road and Changjie, claiming that they would not stop until they achieved their goal of crossing the river. The residents near the Provincial Government and Hanyangmen felt that this action by the students was purely driven by patriotism and could not bear to stand by. As a result, all stores and households opened their doors all night, automatically providing tea and water. The Cao Xiangtai rice store even purchased a large batch of biscuits to comfort them. This shows that popular sentiment is aroused, and the desire to save the country and survive is a common feeling.

While the students were petitioning the Provincial Government, another group of more than 500 people was sent to the upper and lower wharves of Xujiapeng. A group was stationed at Pinghumen, and they all contacted the students at Hanyangmen, waiting for the ferry to start. However, the ferry was ordered to sail elsewhere, and no boats were available. They then negotiated with the Construction Department again and contacted the Hunan-Hubei Railway Bureau in Xujiapeng to dispatch transportation, but both were unsuccessful. Even the boatmen feared interference from the military police and avoided them as much as possible. Therefore, traffic in Wuhan was completely cut off on the 21st. The students who stayed at the Provincial Government waited until 3:00 PM, when Acting Chairman Lu Zhu and Education Director Cheng Qibao received student representatives. The representatives made three requests:

1. Request that the Central Government be notified and declare the true relationship and establishment process of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council to the Central Government.

2. Request that the Central Government be notified, protect the patriotic student movement in Peiping, punish the military and police perpetrators, and release the arrested students.

3. Request that the Provincial Government protect the Wuhan student movement and order the Construction Department to restore the Wuhan ferry service so that they can cross the river for the march.

Lu Zhu replied that the first two points would be forwarded to the Central Government, and the third point of protecting the students was also not a problem, but the restoration of the ferry service would have to be requested from the Pacification Headquarters. It was rumored that Chen Shi, the president of China University, mediated the matter and agreed to allow the students to cross the river in batches for the march on the 22nd and 23rd. The student representatives were responsible for strictly observing discipline to avoid affecting public order. The students considered the result satisfactory and returned to school in formation.

When students in Hankou initially heard that students in Wuchang were blocked and camped out by the river, to help in aid, at noon on the 21st, they continued to gather in Yiyuan for a large-scale march. It is estimated that over two thousand people from ten schools, including Municipal No. 1 Boys' High School, Municipal No. 1 Girls' High School, Xinmian Girls' High School, Yixun Girls' High School, Peiwen Middle School, Luoyi Girls' High School, Jianghan Middle School, Hanjiang Middle School, Aurora Middle School, and Municipal Vocational School, participated. Ye Diya of the Municipal Vocational School served as the commander-in-chief, and Lai Shenxiong of Municipal No. 1 Boys' High School and Zhou Jueshan of Municipal No. 1 Girls' High School served as the deputy commanders.

As they were about to set off, all the students from four schools in Hanyang, including Hanyang Provincial High School of Technology, Hanyang Girls' Vocational School, Hanyang Middle School, and Yizhi Middle School, crossed the Xiang River to Hankou. All students from the Education College and its attached high school in Wuchang, who were blocked, found civilian boats several miles down from Xujiapeng Wharf to cross the river and participate, increasing their momentum. After the march, they went to the Pacification Commissioner's Office to see He Chengjun and petition. They nominated Commander Ye Diya, Zhou Jueshan, and Lai Zhongxiong, and student representatives Yang Zhuai, Xu Qingfeng, and Wang Shufeng from Hanyang, and Zhu Quanji, a representative from the Education College in Wuchang, and eight representatives from Yizhi Middle School to be received. After He Chengjun met with them, he advised them, and the representatives then left the office and announced the disbandment to the public and returned to school. After the students left the office, He Chengjun immediately convened an emergency meeting of responsible persons from the Provincial Government, including Director Wu Guozhen, to discuss maintaining order. Several ferries operated in Wuhan that night, and traffic gradually returned to normal. (21st)

Fujian Province Agricultural Improvement Plan 89

Rural Cooperative Association Organizes Farmer Loans / Agricultural and Forestry Improvement General Field Works Very Actively

Fuzhou dispatch: In order to develop agriculture and forestry, the Fujian Provincial Government has established a Rural Cooperative Committee, sending personnel to various counties to organize rural cooperative societies and organize farmer loans. A total of 1.5 million yuan was loaned out in 1934, all provided by the Farmers' Bank of China. 500,000 yuan has already been loaned out in 1935. Currently, the Rural Cooperative Committee, considering that it is cold and the end of the year, and poor farmers generally urgently need money, has specifically borrowed 200,000 yuan from the Farmers' Bank of China, distributed to rural cooperative societies in nearby counties, and loaned to farmers. 180,000 yuan to Minhou, and 10,000 yuan each to Pingtan and Fuqing.

In order to carry out winter national labor service, the Department of Construction has designated 18 counties, including Minhou, Fuding, Shouning, Pingnan, Minqing, Youxi, Anxi, Zhaoan, Changtai, Haicheng, Yunxiao, Dongshan, Ningyang, Huaan, Qingliu, Mingxi, Songxi, and Zhenghe, and the Fujian-Southern Fujian Fuzhou-Xinghua-Quanzhou, Fujian-Northern Fujian Pu-Ou-Yan, and Fujian-Western Fujian Zhang-Long-Ting three-line highways, as afforestation areas. The committee is limited to complete the work by the end of next March and report it to the department. Personnel will be dispatched to inspect and provide guidance. It has also been decided to hold citrus fruit evaluation meetings in Fuzhou and Zhangzhou on the 15th day of the first lunar month to improve quality. As for the establishment of agricultural improvement facilities, an agency has been established, namely the Provincial Agricultural and Forestry Improvement General Field, which is completely government-run, divided into general affairs, forestry, and agriculture three departments, and attached with two agricultural farms in Changle and Zhangpu, two forest fields in Fuzhou and Nanping, a seedling field in Fuzhou, and a tea field in Fuan.

The Changle agricultural farm focuses on rice cultivation and experiments and research on breeding work. The Zhangpu agricultural farm focuses on experiments and research on horticultural crops such as sugarcane, sweet potatoes, citrus, oranges, and bananas. The Fuan tea farm focuses on improving and breeding tea varieties, and researching improved tea-making methods. The Nanping forest field focuses on afforestation and improving seedling varieties, and researching the utilization of wood. The Fuzhou forest field focuses on experiments and research on forest protection, and research on the planting of coastal windbreak and sand fixation forests.

Those currently being organized include the Provincial Agricultural Improvement Association, which is jointly organized by technicians from the Department of Construction responsible for agricultural and forestry undertakings, and teachers from agricultural and forestry schools in the province, divided into four groups: general affairs, research, promotion, and investigation. And designated four types of rice, fruit trees, seedlings, and livestock as the current main agricultural work in the province. Each type has a design committee responsible for its responsibilities. Currently, the heads of each group and the design committee members have been selected, and the association affairs can be started immediately, and the steps are determined to be first investigation, second research, third experiment, and fourth promotion. (December 21)

Sights and Sounds on the Journey West 91

— Ji Yuan

Miscellaneous Writings on the Chengdu-Chongqing Road

On the morning of October 15th, the reporter braved the rain and took a long-distance public bus from Chongqing to Chengdu. Accompanying me was Mr. Yuan Wenbin. Beforehand, there was much hesitation about taking the bus. Although the Chengdu-Chongqing Highway has a Highway Bureau, the management of vehicles seems to lack thoroughness. The "Special Express" of the Highway Bureau has no fixed schedule, and private car companies and "wild chicken" cars each solicit passengers. The fares are neither fixed nor is there sufficient safety guarantee. In addition, the eastern section of the Chengdu-Chongqing road is muddy due to continuous autumn rains, and there are frequent warnings of overturned vehicles, adding a layer of worry to us. Finally, we mustered our courage and took the Highway Bureau's public bus westward.

That day, we arrived at the bus station outside Tongyuanmen early in the morning to wait for the bus. When we arrived, the first few rows of seats were already occupied, but there were still very few passengers at the station. The reporter asked the reason, and was told, "These are seats reserved by the wife of a certain chief of staff. The wife and others will be here soon." After negotiation, a seat was finally made available in the front row.

The bus was originally scheduled to depart at 7:00 AM, but it was past 9:00 AM when it officially departed, exceeding the scheduled time by more than two hours. Later, it was learned that various transportation agencies and groups in Sichuan often do not adhere to time for gatherings and banquets. For example, for a banquet, the scheduled time is 9:00 AM or 3:00-4:00 PM, but guests always arrive more than half an hour late. It is said that this is to show the guest's high status, not comparable to those who arrive at the first call. This custom has not changed to this day, and the conservatism of the Sichuan people's lifestyle can be seen from this.

When the bus leaves Chongqing city, it must go through a strict inspection, overturning boxes and overturning baskets. Passengers complained endlessly, but the inspectors at the inspection station did not inspect the luggage of "guests" or "military personnel" much. Because the reporter had a letter of introduction from the Highway Bureau, I was also spared some inspection trouble. Ashamed, ashamed.

About sixty li west of Chongqing is the foot of Lao Yingyan Mountain. The bus must spiral up the mountain from here. The mountain road is entirely man-made, and some places must be chiseled through the mountain. The engineering design is very grand, and the terrain is also very majestic, making it the most magnificent part of Sichuan's highway construction. The bus takes about an hour to spiral from the foot of the mountain to the top. When you reach the top, the highway lines you have traveled when spiraling up the mountain can be seen clearly. The scenery is beautiful, difficult to describe. However, the mountain is high and the ground is low, and looking down is quite frightening.

The area on the top of Lao Yingyan Mountain is quite wide. The bus travels here, winding and twisting, surrounded by lush forests, with scattered villages. When going down the mountain, it must still spiral down, and the dangerous situation is even worse than when going up the mountain. Because the turning points are all cut cliffs, although a few piles of earth, low walls, and huge rocks are placed by the roadside for defense, if the driver is even slightly careless, there is still a risk of overturning. After passing Lao Yingyan, you reach Qingmuguan. The plains are quite vast. I heard that there are hot springs, originating from the same source as the Northern Hot Springs, but they have not been utilized. At half past twelve, the bus passed Bishan County. At that time, the drizzle was still pattering. The road was muddy, but fortunately the driver was experienced and able to overcome the dangers as if walking on flat ground. Everywhere we passed, we saw fields crisscrossing, hills undulating, and crops planted all over the mountain tops and roadsides. The neatness of the fields and the diligence of the farmers are rarely seen in other provinces. It is a pity that Sichuan farmers have been exploited by warlords, bureaucrats, local bullies, and landlords for twenty years, shedding tears and swallowing their voices, and their lives are unbearably difficult. Therefore, they all have a haggard look, their clothes are tattered, and seven or eight out of ten rural houses are built of straw and mud walls. The houses with brick walls and tile roofs are mostly buildings from thirty or forty years ago, and there are signs of collapse. The decline of the rural economy can be seen from this. That night, because the road was muddy, the bus traveled very slowly, and we stayed at the Linchun Inn in Rongchang. Almost the entire night was plagued by bed bugs and mosquitoes.

Rongchang, Longchang and other counties are famous for producing summer cloth in Sichuan. The quality is excellent. Years ago, it was sold in various counties in the province and in Guizhou, Yunnan, Shaanxi, Hubei, and other provinces. In recent years, due to the sharp decline in rural purchasing power and the influx of foreign goods, the sales of Rongchang summer cloth have plummeted, and those engaged in the business have a difficult time maintaining it. Therefore, they have to lower prices to solicit business, with each foot priced at just over ten cents. However, the entrances of various summer cloth shops are still deserted. Fortunately, the expenses of each store are not very large, so there are very few closures.

The next morning, we departed from Rongchang to Longchang. The wife of a certain military chief of staff on the bus had an opium addiction. Every time the bus stopped at a location for a longer period, she had to look for a place selling "Sichuan medicine" to indulge in opium. It took about one or two hours before she came back slowly, delaying the travel time considerably. The other passengers felt very unhappy. After passing Longchang, the crops on both sides became another sight. The plains and plateaus were mostly planted with sugarcane, which is the famous sugar-producing area of Neijiang, Sichuan. It is said that Neijiang sugarcane can be divided into red and white varieties, and white sugarcane is further divided into rush hair sugarcane and luohan sugarcane. Most sugarcane farmers are poor, and they cultivate the land as tenants. They pay five to nine yuan in rent per 10,000 catties of sugarcane, and they borrow money mostly with sugarcane as collateral. Every 10,000 catties of sugarcane can be used to borrow twenty to thirty yuan. In the future, the loan will be repaid with the price of sugarcane, and the interest ranges from 2.5% to 4-5% per month. If the sugarcane paid is not enough to repay the loan, the sugar factory has the priority to collect the sugarcane in the coming year.

In recent years, the sales of the sugar industry have been sluggish. The export of Sichuan granular sugar reached 27 million catties in the 21st year, but by the 23rd year, it had decreased by more than two-thirds. Domestic sales have also reportedly decreased by one-half. The underlying reasons are: (A) excessive transportation costs and heavy taxes; (B) easy to damage and unclean; (C) unable to compete with foreign sugar. The methods of improvement should start from improving manufacturing methods, reducing taxes and transportation costs, and expanding sales.

Neijiang is a city with an ancient and elegant style. The streets are quite clean, with willows planted on both sides. Compared with Chongqing, it has a different flavor. The customs of the people are simple and honest, and the market transactions have very little clamor and chaos. The buildings are very low, quite similar to Beijing, and it already has the scenery of Chengdu. This place is 500 li from Chongqing and 580 li from Chengdu. It can be said to be the midpoint on the Chengdu-Chongqing road, and it is also the most commercially prosperous, most populous, and most well-equipped place with hotels and restaurants in the counties along the Chengdu-Chongqing road.

After staying in Neijiang for two hours, the bus continued to move forward. Mr. Yuan, who was traveling with us, was very tired because he was not used to the bumping. After passing Neijiang, the road gradually dried up. Asking the local farmers, we learned that it had not rained in the area west of Neijiang for several days, and the climate was cooler and more comfortable, unlike Chongqing, which was shrouded in mist and drizzle all day long. At 3:00 PM, we passed Zizhong, which is also famous for producing sugar. At 5:00 PM, we passed Ziyang. At this time, it was already twilight. Because we had to rush to Jianzhou for the night, the bus continued to move forward. Sichuan porters generally work day and night, so even late at night, there is a constant stream of porters coming and going on the road. These people mostly make a living by portering, carrying goods, mostly local crude products and agricultural products. Others, such as cigarettes, etc., are also quite common. At about 8:00 PM, the bus arrived in Jianzhou and stayed at the Linlongbin Inn. This place is only 180 li from Chengdu.

From Jianzhou to Chengdu, you have to pass through Shijing Temple. After a brief tour of Shijing Temple, we got on the bus. From then on, the bus gradually went uphill, passing through Longquan驿. The mountain is not very high, but it is quite winding. The bus travels through it, winding up and winding down, not as spiral-shaped as Lao Yingyan. It is said that it is thirty li uphill and thirty li downhill. When you reach the top of Longquan驿 Mountain, you can see the city of Chengdu clearly. Looking far away, the plains are vast and boundless. From Chongqing to the foot of Longquan驿 Mountain, the whole way is undulating hills. At this point, it is an endless plain, as if entering another realm, and the mind is refreshed.

On the third day, at about 11:00 AM, the bus arrived in Chengdu. The first thing that caught my eye was the towering new blockhouses, and the particularly eye-catching bandit suppression slogans. The reporter had already seen blockhouses densely distributed when I traveled upstream along the river. However, seven or eight out of ten were built of mud, not very strong, and the work was simple. Blockhouses were also built along the Chengdu-Chongqing road to prevent banditry. The blockhouses built outside Chengdu city are all made of bricks, the construction is strong, and the form is also very magnificent, but the cost is said to be quite high. Mr. Yuan Wenbin said that the blockhouses built in the suburbs of major cities in Jiangxi are also more magnificent than those built in the countryside.

Xiao He's Communist Bandits are Rampant; Guangdong Province Deploys Border Defense; The Second Army Headquarters Moves to Shao to Facilitate Command 92

Guangzhou Dispatch: Xiao He's communist bandits have recently fled into Guizhou and Guangxi. One group entered Guizhou and is currently ravaging eastern Guizhou. More than 10,000 communist bandits attacked Zhenyuan on the 7th. The defending 93rd Division, led by Gan Lichu, met them in battle. After a fierce battle all night, Gan's troops decided to consolidate their defense at Zhenxiongguan on the 8th as part of a change in strategy. The communist bandits suffered heavy casualties in Zhenyuan. Currently, Guo Siyuan's troops have reinforced Zhenxiong, and Shangguan Yunxiang's division has also joined the blocking effort. The Guangxi army has moved to Guyi, Yongquan, Longsheng, and Ningyi. Bai Chongxi plans to go to Guilin to command. Because it is rumored that a unit of communist bandits from western Hunan has been discovered in northern Guangxi, the Guilin militia has also been mobilized. At the same time, Beijiang in Guangdong Province, which borders Hunan, is also actively deploying defenses. The various units of the First Army have been ordered to strengthen their defense deployments in their original garrisons and strictly prevent the activities of local communists. Deputy Army Commander Li Zhenqiu departed from Dayu on the 9th to inspect the defenses of various departments along the Jiangxi border and instruct the regimental commanders on bandit suppression. As for the defense of the Xiangbian area, the 4th Division of the Second Army, led by Wu Jianxiong, was dispatched to Lechang, Pingshi, Xingzi, and other places some days ago, choosing strategic locations to guard and ordering his troops to scout for communist bandits' movements at any time. During this winter defense period, anyone entering Guangdong from Xiangbian with suspicious behavior will be interrogated. Only those recognized as legitimate merchants will be allowed to pass through. The Second Army Headquarters was originally located in the provincial capital, but recently, in order to facilitate command, the army headquarters was also moved to Shaoguan. Chen Jitang, commander of the Second Army, personally went to the army headquarters on the 7th to give a speech to the officers, encouraging his subordinates to be public-spirited, abide by the law, cooperate with the people, and maintain local security. The army headquarters' staff, adjutant, military supplies, ordnance, military medical departments, and directly subordinate units, engineering battalion, special service company, machine gun company, communications platoon, etc., began to relocate to Shaoguan in batches from the 9th. The directly subordinate units and baggage went first, and the chief of staff led the members to depart, arriving in Shaoguan that evening. The army headquarters was located in the Guangzhou Guild Hall in Shaocheng, and it opened for business as usual the next day. Zhang Da, deputy commander of the Second Army, is scheduled to go to Shao on the 14th to convene a meeting of the subordinate division and regimental commanders to discuss the deployment of border defenses. (December 13th)

Songjiang

Dispute Arises from Gun Inspection Case

Wang Mingfu, the director of the Ruose Hospital in this city, recently followed the order of the county government to hand over the gun to Jin Gentang, the head of Xiao Qianjing Township, for registration. After receiving the license, he took the gun back to Ruose Hospital, intending to hand it over to Wang Minfu. Suddenly, three people, including a certain Zhu, stepped forward to inspect it. Township Head Jin first showed them the gun license issued by the county government, but they wanted Township Head Jin to hand over the already marked pistol, so a dispute arose. They overturned the registration counter of the hospital, causing the patients to lose color and flee in panic. In the examination room, Sun Deji was having an intravenous injection. The doctor's hands trembled when he saw the police, and blood flowed profusely, posing a dangerous situation. Later, two officials, Lang Yinong and Yang Jingjiang, were dispatched by the district office and the Public Security Bureau to stop the dispute. They sent all the witnesses to the Public Security Bureau for disposal. It is said that the Ruose Hospital felt aggrieved for being humiliated for no reason as a charitable organization. On the 22nd, they specially presented a petition to the county party headquarters, the county government, and the Public Security Bureau, requesting an investigation, and ordering the surrender of the fleeing offender who carried the gun and compensation for the loss.

Suzhou

Students Parade and Distribute Proclamations to the People

More than 500 students from Suzhou High School here on the 22nd were divided into nine teams. The student National Salvation Association organized by the student union was responsible for convening the students. At 10:00 AM, they gathered in the Zhongshan Hall of Wu Miaoguan, and then went to the bustling areas inside and outside the city to publicize. They distributed proclamations to the people and letters to all students in Suzhou along the way. The Public Security Bureau sent plainclothes detectives to protect them and to guard outside the Japanese concession and in front of the Japanese shops on Banmen Avenue to prevent petty thieves from taking the opportunity to make trouble and causing accidents. The local order was very peaceful.

Changzhou

The City Cracks Down on Extortionist Criminals

Liu Wei, a lawyer in Zhouxian Lane in Wuyi City, received a letter from a soldier through a maid at about 8:00 PM on the 18th of this month, instructing her to give it to a stranger. Liu Wei opened it and learned that he was being threatened to extort 300 yuan in silver dollars, to be placed in a nearby trash can covered with vegetable leaves at 10:30 PM on the 20th. If he did not comply, they would use force to set fire and kill people, etc., and an attached bullet. Liu Wei reported it to Si Daoping, the director of the Public Security First Sub-bureau, on the 19th. It was agreed to use grass paper and attach two yuan in foreign currency and write a reply on a piece of paper, wrapped in newspaper, and placed in the manner mentioned in the threatening letter. After the deployment, Director Si, Inspector Chen Rui, and other police officers went to wait at about 9:00 PM on the 20th. Director Si disguised as a rickshaw driver, and Chen Rui disguised as a worker, ambushing nearby. At that time, a soldier was seen taking a paper package from the trash can and putting it in his coat pocket. Director Si and others rushed forward and captured him, taking him to the bureau. It was found that his name was Wang Shaofu, who had served in the security team before. The bureau, considering that such a case had occurred in the city, sent him to the general bureau and transferred him to the county government for trial on the 21st.

Zhenjiang

Remedial Measures for Investigating Opium Offenders

The Provincial Anti-Opium Association believes that it is often difficult to be accurate in the investigation of opium offenders transferred by the opium addiction rehabilitation centers in various counties to the provincial government. There are often cases where fellow villagers know that someone is addicted to opium, but the investigation finds that they are not addicted. Now that the general inspection is about to be held, the investigation aspect is becoming increasingly important. Special remedial measures are proposed as follows: Anyone who is reported by someone and the responsible Baojia chief proves that they are indeed using opium, or who is reported by their direct relatives, even if the investigation finds that they are not addicted, will also be considered a suspect. They should be ordered to obtain a solid shop guarantee and guarantor, restricting their residence for one year for long-term observation. If it is discovered that they are using opium, they will be severely punished, and the guarantors will be held jointly liable. Those who cannot find a guarantor will be temporarily detained, and released after it is confirmed that they will not use opium. The above measures have been sent to the provincial government for handling.

Hangzhou

Two Fires Claim Three Lives

At 9:15 PM on the 21st, Yao Hong, a 69-year-old resident of No. 142, Sibao, Hangzhou City, accidentally caused a fire while drying bedding. The fire spread rapidly. The fire brigade and other fire rescue organizations rushed to the scene to extinguish the fire, but three thatched houses had already been burned down. Yao Hong, due to her old age and frailty, was unable to escape and died in the fire along with her two three- or four-year-old grandsons. The loss was more than 200 yuan. Also, at 1:15 PM on the 22nd, the Xinxin Electric Materials Store at No. 37, Chenghuang Archway, caught fire because the store owner, Wang Xiqiu, accidentally caused a fire while drying it. The fire spread to the plank wall, and the wind caused the fire to blaze fiercely. The fire brigade and others tried their best to rescue it, but five stores, including the Jiji Fresh Meat Store, Xie Runtai Store, Changmao Fruit Store, and Tongxing Sauce Garden, were burned down, with a loss of more than 5,000 yuan.

The Special Commissioner's Office of Nantong District, due to repeated robbery cases in various counties, convened a winter defense conference at 7:00 PM on the 20th, bringing together military, government, and police officials.
