Organize guerrilla teams to patrol in three routes; 3. Baojia chiefs must effectively report hidden bandits; 4. Nantong County Magistrate Jin Zonghua should go to various districts in the near future to inspect the organization of the patrol teams.

Education Broadcasting Special Issue

A Simple Explanation of the Human Body's Structure and Functions 93

— Sun Zongpeng, Professor at Central University

Humans are the most advanced animals, and their structure is extremely complex. It is impossible to describe everything in detail in a short time. I will only discuss the general aspects. The composition of various parts of the human body is based on tiny cells as units. A large number of cells combine to form tissues, tissues form organs, and organs form systems. Each system and organ in the body has its own responsibility, and they cooperate to perform daily life activities. In terms of structure, the human body can be divided into major systems such as muscles, bones, digestion, circulation, nerves, reproduction, excretion, respiration, and endocrine. The structure and function of each system are described below.

(1) Muscular System

The main function of muscles is to control movement and form soft organs in the body. In terms of shape, they can be divided into three types: striated muscle—that is, the muscle that makes up the external shell of the body, attached to the bones to unite the bones, and under the guidance of nerves, to perform conscious movements; smooth muscle—used to make up the internal organs, such as the stomach, intestines, and blood vessels. These organs perform unconscious movements under normal conditions, like a machine that cannot freely stop once it is turned on; cardiac muscle—this kind of muscle has the shape of striated muscle, but its function is like that of smooth muscle. It is used to make up the heart. The inside of the muscles is full of tiny blood vessels to supply nutrients, and there are also nerves to receive external stimuli.

(2) Skeletal System

The skeleton can be divided into two major parts: the trunk and the limbs. The trunk is divided into the head, neck, chest, back, waist, and tail, while the limbs are the hands and feet. The function of the skeleton is to support the posture of the whole body and to protect the internal soft tissues, such as the skull protecting the brain, the vertebrae protecting the spinal cord, the chest and ribs forming the chest cavity to protect the heart and lungs, and the lumbar vertebrae supporting the abdominal cavity to protect the stomach and intestines. In terms of texture, bones can be divided into cartilage and hard bone. Children have more cartilage because it is not yet calcified. The degree of calcification increases with age, and when people are old, the bones are brittle due to the high amount of calcium (commonly known as lime). Therefore, broken bones are not easy to heal in old age.

(3) Digestive System

The path from the mouth to the anus is called the digestive tract, including the oral cavity, pharynx, esophagus, stomach, small intestine, large intestine, rectum, etc. In addition, there are accessory glands such as the liver and pancreas. At the junction of the small and large intestines, there is a cecum. The main function of this system is to digest food to nourish the body. In addition to vitamins and inorganic salts, food can be roughly divided into three categories: carbohydrates, that is, sugar, starch, and fiber; proteins, such as animal meat and egg whites; and fats, that is, oils.

After food enters the mouth, the saliva secreted in the mouth digests part of the carbohydrates into sugar, because the saliva contains enzymes that digest carbohydrates. Then, the food enters the stomach through the pharynx and esophagus. The gastric juice contains digestive enzymes, called protein enzymes, fat enzymes, and carbohydrate enzymes, to digest the three types of food. Undigested food is transferred to the small intestine, where it is digested by intestinal juice and enzymes secreted by the pancreas. The bile from the liver is also helpful in digestion. Digested food is absorbed by the intestinal wall and enters the blood, and is distributed to various parts of the body through blood circulation. Undigestible residue is excreted from the body through the large intestine, rectum, and anus. It is not clear what the function of the cecum is in the human body, but in lower animals such as rabbits, the cecum contains bacteria, which do participate in some of the work, because a kind of bacteria ferments, which can make food easier to digest.

(4) Circulatory System

The circulatory system includes blood circulation and lymph circulation. The blood circulatory system includes the heart, arteries, veins, and spleen. The spleen is a lymphatic gland that is closely related to red blood cells and hemoglobin. The heart is divided into left and right atria and left and right ventricles. The walls of the ventricles are thicker than those of the atria. The contraction of the ventricles can generate pressure, causing blood to flow into the arteries and be distributed throughout the body. The walls of the arteries are thicker than those of the veins, so they can withstand stronger pressure. The direction of blood flow in the arteries is centrifugal, while the veins are the opposite. The farther the blood vessels are from the heart, the finer the branches. The circulation of blood starts from the left ventricle and enters the arteries, distributing throughout the body, and then enters the right atrium through the veins, turns into the right ventricle, and is input into the lungs. In this way, the turbid blood is exchanged for gas through breathing to make the blood clear, and then input from the lungs into the left atrium and into the left ventricle, and the action of heart contraction makes the blood re-enter the arteries to circulate.

Blood contains tiny blood cells, which can be roughly divided into two types: red and white. Red blood cells contain hemoglobin, hence the name, and are rich in the characteristic of absorbing oxygen. White blood cells are generally smaller than red blood cells and have different shapes, and have the characteristic of resisting or eliminating bacteria. In addition, there are platelets. In addition to distributing nutrients and heat, blood also has the characteristic of resisting toxins. Lymphatic vessels run along the blood vessels, and the vessels contain lymph, which is milky white because it contains nutrients. Lymph is actually the main organ for absorbing nutrients, and the nutrients in the blood are derived from lymph.

(5) Nervous System

The nervous system is the only main organ that transmits stimuli and directs movements of the whole body. Physiologically, it can be divided into sensory nerves and motor nerves. In terms of location, it can be divided into the central nervous system and the peripheral nervous system. The central nervous system is divided into two major parts: the brain and the spinal cord, which are hollow and have fluid. The peripheral nerves are the nerves that emanate from the brain and spinal cord and are distributed around the body to make contact with the outside world. There are twelve pairs of cranial nerves and a number of spinal nerves. Anatomically, the brain of the central nervous system can be divided into the cerebrum, midbrain, cerebellum, pons, and medulla oblongata. Humans are the highest animals, so the cerebrum is particularly developed. Because the skull limits it, it cannot extend outward, but increases the area inward, so there are a number of wrinkles on it. The cerebrum is divided into two parts: the forebrain and the interbrain. The forebrain controls the sensation and voluntary movement of the whole body, understanding, memory, thinking, association, and other noble functions. The first pair of cranial nerves (olfactory nerves) originate from this part. The interbrain is behind the forebrain and is the general meeting place for sensory stimuli of the whole body. It also controls reflex movements. The second pair of cranial nerves (optic nerves) and the third pair of cranial nerves (oculomotor nerves) originate from this part. The midbrain controls vision and hearing, and reflex movements of the body. The fourth pair of cranial nerves (oculomotor nerves) originate from this part. The cerebellum controls the muscle movement of the whole body, regulates the balance of the whole body, and the coordination of muscles. The pons is embedded in the cerebellum, and controls the sensation of facial skin, the sensation of all muscles in the head, taste, and the movement of chewing, and the secretion of sweat glands and salivary glands. The last is the medulla oblongata, which controls reflection and adjustment work. In addition, it controls the movement of internal organs, such as breathing, vomiting, and swallowing. The fifth to twelfth pairs of cranial nerves originate from this part. Behind the medulla oblongata is the spinal cord, which controls the reception of external stimuli and reflex movements of the trunk and limbs. Spinal nerves originate from this. In addition, there are sympathetic nerves, which come from the nerve knots of the spinal nerves and reach the internal organs, controlling the movement of smooth muscle and cardiac muscle. In addition to the nerves mentioned above, there are sensory organs to receive external stimuli, which are transmitted from the peripheral nerves to the central nervous system. The sensory organs will be briefly described below.

Visual organ: The eye controls vision and is spherical. The front of the eye has a transparent cornea, inside which is the anterior chamber, which contains transparent liquid. Behind the chamber is the iris, which has a hole called the pupil. The lens is attached to the back of the pupil. In the human body, the lens is elliptical. Behind the lens is the posterior chamber, which also contains liquid. Light comes from the outside and penetrates the cornea, passes through the liquid in the anterior and posterior chambers, and is projected onto the retina inside to obtain an image. The principle is like that of a camera, so it is not difficult to understand. The retina is composed of optic nerves, which is the most important part of vision. It contains cells that distinguish light and color. Except for the front part, which is covered with the cornea, the outer layer of the eyeball is a cartilaginous body called the sclera, and the inner layer is the retina. Between the sclera and the retina are the choroid and the choroid membrane.

Auditory organ: The ear controls hearing and is divided into four parts: the auricle, the external auditory canal, the middle ear, and the inner ear. Between the middle ear and the external auditory canal is the tympanic membrane. Behind the tympanic membrane are three small bones. Sound waves hit the tympanic membrane and are transmitted into the ear. Between the ear and the oral cavity, there is the Eustachian tube, which connects to the inner ear through two small holes. The structure of the inner ear is extremely complex, with tortuous ducts embedded in the auditory bone. Both inside and outside the ducts have lymphatic fluid. The ducts are divided into three semicircular canals that control balance and the cochlea that has hearing, to which the auditory nerves are attached.

Olfactory organ: The nose controls smell. The walls of the nasal cavity are covered with olfactory nerve cells. The nasal cavity communicates with the oral cavity, so the nose also controls breathing.

Gustatory organ: The tongue controls taste. Its surface has a number of protrusions, which contain taste cells connected to the taste nerves.

Tactile organ: The skin controls touch, so the whole body has this function, but the fingers are the most sensitive. In addition to touch, it also controls cold, heat, pain, etc. (To be continued)

After the Promulgation of the Sino-French-Vietnamese Treaty, Vietnam Imposes Heavy Import Duties on Chinese Silk 97

In addition to the regular tax and capital tax, a balancing tax is also levied. The silk industry and others petition the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for negotiations with France.

According to Hua Dong News Agency, the Shanghai Electrical Machinery Silk Weaving Industry and the Silk Fabric Industry Associations jointly submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that after the promulgation and implementation of the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty, Chinese silk sales to Vietnam should enjoy the lowest tax rate according to the attached schedule. However, the Vietnamese customs are creating tax items arbitrarily, arbitrarily assessing prices, and levying heavy taxes, which are heavier than the taxes paid during the period without a treaty. Overseas Chinese merchants are suffering greatly, and the sales of Chinese silk are on the verge of extinction. They urgently petition the association, earnestly requesting a swift and serious negotiation with the French government to cancel any surtaxes other than those stipulated in the commercial treaty, to comply with the original intention of reciprocity, and to help with foreign trade. It is noted that before 1926, the annual sales of Chinese silk imported into Annam reached more than 10 million yuan. Since the establishment of a commercial treaty between our country and Annam during the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty, Chinese silk enjoyed the most-favored-nation tax rate. Therefore, silk sales to Vietnam were very prosperous at that time. In July 1927, the Sino-Vietnamese commercial treaty expired, and the silk imported by our country had to be treated the same as countries without a treaty for ordinary taxation. Only one type of regular tax was levied. Since then, in addition to the regular tax, a capital tax (similar to our country's business tax) has to be added. Since then, the burden on overseas Chinese has increased, and the sales of Chinese silk have been greatly hit. In 1930, Wang Zhengting, our former Minister of Foreign Affairs, and the French envoy Martel, negotiated a special treaty, but due to the relationship between Schedules A and B, the French side delayed approval, and it has been suspended until now for several years. During this period, the export of Chinese silk to Vietnam was almost completely extinct, and the business of overseas Chinese and the export of domestic silk merchants both suffered. On May 4th of this year, the Sino-French-Vietnamese treaty was fortunately announced. When Chinese silk continued to be transported to Vietnam, it was expected that the old foundation would be rebuilt, but suddenly urgent letters were received from the Annam Di'an and Xidi silk fabric industry associations, stating that since the promulgation of the commercial treaty, the Vietnamese customs has not only failed to reduce the import tax rate on Chinese silk, but has increased it compared to the period without a treaty, and has created many names to impose heavy taxes and levies arbitrarily. Taking Chinese silk as an example, only regular tax was levied in the old treaty to show preferential treatment. Later, when there was no treaty, according to the ordinary tax rate, a capital tax had to be added in addition to the regular tax. Now that a new treaty has been established, the capital tax should be abolished immediately to comply with the principle of reciprocity. However, recently, the Vietnamese customs has not only failed to remove the capital tax, but has also added a balancing tax, which is levied at 25% of the assessed value. For example, for every 100 kilograms of crepe-faced light-colored pure silk fabrics imported into Annam, the comparison of the old and new tax rates is as follows: A. Tax rate under the old treaty (regular tax): 1,360 francs. B. Tax rate without a treaty (regular tax): 10,000 francs; capital tax: 900 francs; total: 10,900 francs. C. Tax rate recently promulgated by the commercial treaty: regular tax: 8,500 francs; capital tax: 537.5 francs; balancing tax: 2,250 francs; total: 11,287.5 francs. According to the above examples, it can be proved that after the new treaty was signed, the Vietnamese customs' import tax rate on Chinese silk was not only heavier than that collected under the old treaty, but also more than that collected under the ordinary tax rate without a treaty. The added balancing tax, although claimed to be 25%, is assessed according to the exchange rate, which is actually an arbitrary floating assessment without any standards, and sometimes it is even levied at 50%. The capital tax is calculated by adding all costs and taxes paid, and then assessing the value, which is taxation within taxation. Therefore, the value of import taxes on Chinese silk is generally between 100% and 150% of the value. Overseas Chinese merchants cannot afford such harsh taxes and levies. If Chinese silk wants to be exported to Vietnam, its livelihood will be cut off. The association cannot remain silent in the face of such pain, so it submits this petition. It is hoped that the Executive Yuan and the Ministry will review and approve it, and promptly lodge a serious protest with the French government. All surtaxes other than those stipulated in the official treaty and the attached schedule should be stopped. It must also be guaranteed that no new taxes will be created and no floating taxes will be collected in the future. The regular tax levied should also be noted and should not be higher than the import tax of non-reciprocal countries, to comply with the principle of the lowest tax rate in the attached schedule, so as to realize the spirit of reciprocity in the treaty. If the French side delays and ignores the negotiations, it seems that our government can also levy other additional taxes on coal, rice and other items transported from Annam to our country to show retaliation. It is appropriate to decide, I am trembling to await orders, in addition to the attached comparative table of tax rates, respectfully submitted.

Explanation: From May 1926, the tax was increased from 200 francs to 800 francs per 100 kilograms. After October of the same year, it was increased to 1,360 francs. From July 1927, in addition to the regular tax in the previous clause, a capital tax of 2% of the value was added, based on a minimum valuation of 18,000 francs per 100 kilograms, with a tax of 360 francs per 100 kilograms. From July 1929, the Sino-French commercial treaty expired, and our country lost the most-favored-nation tax rules and was treated according to the ordinary tax rate of countries without a treaty. In January 1933, the capital tax was increased to 5% of the value. On August 8, 1935, the new tax rules were implemented, and the regular tax was slightly reduced, but the capital tax was not abolished. The French side created another name for the balancing tax. Combining the various tax items, it was not only not reduced, but heavier than the tax paid without a treaty.

Ministry of Finance Adjusts the Banking System 98

Central Bank to be Reorganized into a Reserve Bank; Mint to Start Minting Decimal Subsidiary Coins

According to Central News Agency, after the Ministry of Finance implemented the new currency system policy, it is determined to adjust the domestic banking system. The first step is to reorganize the Central Bank into the Central Reserve Bank. After the resolution of the plenary meeting of the board of directors, 40% of commercial shares will be raised. The matter has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The Central Mint is minting decimal subsidiary coins. After the promulgation of the subsidiary coin regulations, minting will begin. After the reporter learned about the situation, the details are recorded below.

Reserve Bank Submitted to the Executive Yuan for Approval

The reorganization of the Central Bank into the Central Reserve Bank was approved by the plenary meeting of the bank's board of directors last month. According to Article 7 of the current Central Bank Law, 40% of the commercial shares will be raised (the bank's current capital is 100 million yuan). The matter has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. At the same time, preparations for reorganization are being actively planned. It can be implemented as soon as the order from the Executive Yuan is received. In the future, all ordinary banking businesses of the bank, such as remittance, mortgage, trust savings, etc., will be transferred to specialized banks for exclusive operation, and the businesses of various banks will be adjusted according to their nature. The Ministry of Finance will also appoint experts from the Economic Research Department of the Central Bank to various banks to supervise and assist in the improvement of their businesses.

Decimal Subsidiary Coins to be Minted Soon

After the implementation of the new currency system policy, the national currency standard system has been unified. The consolidation of subsidiary coins is currently under study. The subsidiary coin models ordered by the Central Mint from the United States have been shipped, and trials are currently underway. It is planned to have five types of copper-nickel silver subsidiary coins, including one cent, five cents, one jiao, two jiao, and five jiao. As soon as the central government promulgates the subsidiary coin regulations, minting will begin. An important declaration will be issued soon.

At 12:00 PM, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce hosted a banquet for Zou Lu at its meeting room in Tianhougong Bridge to show their connection. Central Committee members Hu Wencan, Xu Jiyin, Wang Yansong, Luo Qinghua, Zheng Zenan, Wang Zhisheng, and Chang Mumin, among others, were invited to accompany him. The chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, Xu Jiyin, presided over the banquet, and the conversation was very enjoyable. At 1:00 PM in the afternoon, Zou Lu continued to Shenxin No. 9 Factory on Macao Road to attend a banquet hosted by Rong Zongjing. He then visited the factory and Fuxin No. 2 and No. 8 Flour Mills. The Mayor of Shanghai, Wu Tiecheng, also hosted a banquet for Zou Lu at his private residence on Haig Road yesterday evening at 7:00 PM, inviting Central Committee member Hu Wencan, Jianghai Customs Superintendent Tang Haian, and many others to accompany him. Sun Ke, President of the Legislative Yuan, is scheduled to host a farewell banquet for him at his private residence tonight. Zou Lu was originally scheduled to depart on the German mail ship "Bosdan" on the 24th, but it has now been decided to postpone it by one day, and he will depart on the American mail ship "President Grant" on the 25th.

A Visit to a 111-Year-Old Woman 104

Such an Elderly Person Encountering Disaster and Displacement; Fortunately, a Great-Grandson Serves Her with Great Care

According to the "North China Daily News," a representative of the newspaper visited Zhang, a 111-year-old woman from Shandong, at the Renji Hospital yesterday (the 21st). The woman is almost blind and has lost all her teeth, but she is still in good physical condition and can get out of bed without assistance. Although her memory is almost completely gone, she can still understand the Shandong dialect and express her needs. The woman usually lies quietly and does not care much about food. She now mostly relies on liquids such as milk for nourishment. The hospital staff feels sorry for the woman who is so old and displaced and has raised money to help her return to her hometown of Jining. The representative of the "North China Daily News" sat by the old woman's bed and had a short conversation with her, shouting into her ear. The woman said she felt very comfortable. When asked what she wanted to eat, the woman shook her hand and replied, "What food is good to eat?" The woman also said that she came to Shanghai to find relatives but did not find them. She had lived in a village and had never been out before. When the representative asked her about some aspects of her life, the woman only smiled and shook her head frequently. The woman's forehead is wrinkled, but it does not hide her kind face. She always answers warmly to those who talk to her. The woman has only one great-grandson, who is already thirty-two years old. According to a certain doctor, the man serves his great-grandmother carefully and meticulously, which is touching. He is proud to have such an elderly great-grandmother and takes care of her in every possible way. It so happened that the man was also lying ill in the hospital, so the representative was able to ask about his family history and learned that his name was Zhang San. Because of the flood in his hometown, he took the old woman by train to Pukou and came to Shanghai to find his cousin Wen, who worked as a policeman in the Shanghai Public Security Bureau. After boarding the ship in Pukou, all of his luggage was stolen, and one of the old woman's clothes was also inside. The travel expenses of several yuan and the address of his cousin Wen were all sewn into the clothes. Therefore, after arriving in Shanghai, they had no money to buy food and no place to go, so they begged for food. Soon after, the old woman fell ill in the street. Just as they were worried and distressed, a Western patrolman from the Central Police Station happened to pass by, saw them, and took pity on them. After inquiring about everything, he sent the old woman to the hospital. A few days later, Zhang San also fell ill. Zhang San's grandparents and parents had all passed away, and his only relative was his cousin, who was said to be working as a policeman in the Shanghai Public Security Bureau. Zhang San was raised by the old woman since he was an infant. When he grew up, he opened a teahouse for a living. Recently, he lost everything due to the flood. He was overjoyed when he received a letter from his cousin in Shanghai and decided to come to Shanghai to find him. Zhang San recalled that his great-grandmother was born in the fifth year of the Daoguang reign (1825) and became a widow at the age of twenty-one, which is now ninety years ago. Her children and grandchildren had all died early. Zhang San is still a widower and depends on his great-grandmother. He had never left his village before the flood. According to the old woman's birth year, she was born in 1825 by the Gregorian calendar. When she got married, foreigners had just arrived in Shanghai. At that time, the Shanghai Concession was still a desolate area. Counting her life, she has lived through five emperors and entered the Republic of China for twenty-four years. Also, in hospitals, it is common to see babies, but it is rare to see elderly people over eighty years old. Now, Renji Hospital has received the patronage of this elderly woman, which can be considered a hard record to break.

Railway to Collect and Dispatch Postal and Telegraph Items: Three Bureaus Have Agreed on Implementation Measures; Official Implementation Starting Next Month on the 1st, with Postal and Telegraph Fees and Other Details Remaining Unchanged 115

The Ministries of Transportation and Railways are planning for railway stations to collect and dispatch postal and telegraph items for passengers. It has been decided that, starting from the 1st of next month, a trial run will be conducted at nine major stations along the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways. The postal and telegraph bureaus of these two railway lines have already agreed on implementation measures. The details are as follows:

Regarding Telegrams: Major stations that establish telegraph collection and dispatch services will have the railway bureau designate, within a possible scope, two windows—one near the ticket office and one near the platform. This will facilitate the sending and receiving of telegrams by passengers in waiting rooms and on trains. The railway bureau will also assign personnel to collect and dispatch telegrams on the train and deliver telegrams sent by passengers or to passengers on the train. This will allow passengers to communicate with others while traveling. The telegraph fee will be the same as for ordinary telegrams, charged according to regulations, without additional line fees.

Regarding Postal Items: For the sending and receiving of postal items, for example, if a passenger traveling from Shanghai to Nanjing wishes to communicate with Shanghai while passing through Suzhou or Zhenjiang, they can send postal items on the train and have the on-train personnel dispatch them. If someone in Shanghai wants to send something to a passenger on the train, they must specify the train time and the class the passenger is traveling in. The railway bureau's information office will notify the station by telephone to inform the passenger.

Trial Run Next Month: The railway postal and telegraph stations along the railway line have been regulated by the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Railways. The (Beijing-Shanghai Line) Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Changzhou, Wuxi, Shanghai North Station, (Shanghai-Hangzhou Line) Shanghai South Station, Songjiang, Jiaxing, Hangzhou, and other nine major stations under the jurisdiction of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration will conduct a trial run first. The Shanghai Postal General Bureau of the Ministry of Transportation, the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau, and the Railway Ministry's two Railway Administration bureaus have agreed to implement this from January 1, 25th year. Detailed measures for all stations' collection and dispatch of postal and telegraph items will be announced via press release in the coming days.

Special Award Certificate for "Spring of Farmers":凌其翰 Brings It Back Home; Submitted to the China Educational Film Association for Safekeeping; The Two Certificates Have Extraordinary Beautiful Designs 116

During the Belgian government-sponsored Brussels International Exposition this spring, an international rural film competition was held to improve rural life, and China was invited to participate. The China Educational Film Association produced a film called "Spring of Farmers" to participate in the competition and won a special award. The award certificate was handed over to Mr.凌其翰, the chargé d'affaires stationed in Belgium, who brought it back to China and submitted it to the Film Association. There are two certificates: one is the Special Award Certificate for "Spring of Farmers," and the other is a Commemorative Certificate for the Judging Committee. Both are made of high-quality paper and use French and Flemish to write the name of the product, the level of the award, and the producer. The certificates depict two barefoot farm women holding flowers and plants, with a rural village in the background. The sides are inlaid with wheat and roses, and the upper, lower, left, and right corners of the picture depict animal and plant patterns, fully expressing the great significance of agriculture. The upper and lower corners of the picture depict the Expo logo, which is exceptionally beautiful. China's receipt of this special award is a great international honor.

Ministry of Interior Informs the Municipal Government: Police Agencies to Increase Gas Gun Provisions; So That Police Officers Can Perform Their Duties; Immediate Orders to the Public Safety Bureau to Comply 118

According to the Industrial News Agency, the Ministry of Interior, in view of police cases, when the police are performing their duties of apprehending criminals, must consider preserving the lives of the criminals and suspects before the case has been judged. This often results in arresting officers watching the criminals escape or continuing criminal behavior. Even though they have weapons in hand, they find it difficult to enforce prohibition. To remedy this, the Ministry of Interior has adopted scientific police weapon equipment, similar to that used in other countries, and added gas guns to enable police officers to perform their duties. The Ministry yesterday sent a special notice to the municipal government, instructing its affiliated police agencies to uniformly add this type of equipment, and to impart scientific knowledge for its application, to increase the strength of maintaining local security. It is reported that after receiving the order, the municipal government immediately ordered the Public Safety Bureau to comply.

City Public Safety Bureau Submits to the Ministry of Finance: Urging Allocation of Stamp Tax Awards; The Ministry of Finance Has Forwarded the Consultation to the Ministry of Judicial Administration 120

The Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau previously submitted a request to the Municipal Government to forward it to the Ministry of Finance, which in turn forwarded it to the Ministry of Judicial Administration, instructing the local courts to expedite the allocation of public expenses and bonuses that the Bureau had submitted for trial in the stamp tax violation cases, so that they could be allocated to the relevant personnel to reward them. Now, the Ministry of Finance has approved it and approved a consultation to the Ministry of Judicial Administration, instructing the Shanghai Local Court to promptly conclude the cases submitted for trial and to allocate the fines obtained. The original consultation of the Ministry of Finance Tax Character No. 19823 is as follows: It is found that since the stamp tax stamps were changed to be sold by the post office, the responsibility for inspecting stamp matters has been assigned to the municipal and county governments. This matter is purely of an obligatory nature and has no designated funds. In order to subsidize the inspection agencies and reward the inspection personnel, the Ministry has specially stipulated in the Rules for Inspecting Stamp Tax that if there are no informants in the case, 20% of the fines should be used to subsidize the operating expenses of the inspection agency, and 20% should be awarded to the personnel who have made efforts in handling the case. Subsequently, the 20% subsidy obtained by the inspection agency was very small and insufficient for office use. This Ministry has re-approved the agreement of your Ministry to revise the provisions for the distribution of fines in the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax Fines and Execution Rules of the Judicial Organs, stipulating that 40% of the cases obtained by the inspection agency should be used for the operating expenses of the judicial organs, 40% should be used for the operating expenses of the inspection agency, and 20% should be awarded to the personnel who have made efforts in the matter. This case is currently being submitted to the National Government by the Executive Yuan together with the Judicial Yuan for approval. The fines that the inspection agencies and inspection personnel should receive are very important for carrying out the inspection work and should be allocated as soon as they are received for office use. It is also found that in order to improve the methods for the court to hear stamp tax cases, your Ministry has issued a notice to all courts to comply with it. From now on, when handling such cases, except for those with doubts that cannot be concluded without investigation, they should be concluded within three days. The books and records should be returned immediately upon conclusion of the case. The local judicial organs should comply with this. In response to the consultation, a copy of the original consultation and a copy of the original submission are enclosed for your Ministry to review and instruct the Shanghai Local Court to promptly conclude the cases of violations of the Stamp Tax Regulations submitted by the Shanghai Municipal Public Safety Bureau and to send the fines due to the Bureau for distribution. In addition, according to the report of the Stamp Tax Inspection Committee of the Ministry, there are also delays in the trial of cases of violations of stamp tax laws by other judicial organs. Please reiterate the previous order and strictly order that the cases submitted for trial be concluded as soon as they are tried and that the fines received be allocated as soon as they are concluded, so that the stamp inspection work and the use of certificates by merchants and the public will be convenient.

Debt Dispute: Objection Raised to Auction of Real Estate 122

陈耀先, from Chuansha County, Pudong, used to work in the foreign accounts department of Yongxing Foreign Firm. His deceased father and the father of his cousin 陈克扬 were both clansmen and close friends, so financial dealings were common. In 1925, 陈克扬's father borrowed 500 taels of silver from 陈耀先's father. Later, a person named 黄心一, with 陈耀先's father as guarantor, purchased goods from 陈克扬's father, totaling over 490 taels of silver, so the debts were offset at that time. Unexpectedly, after many years, since the death of 陈耀先's father, 陈耀先 suddenly filed a lawsuit in the civil court of the First Special Court in July last year, suing 陈克扬's father to recover the loan of his deceased father. After several court sessions, because the defendant did not arrive, a public announcement was made, and a default judgment was made. It was found that 陈克扬's father also had real estate in Chuansha County, so he applied to the execution court of the First Special Court, requesting that the Chuansha County Government assist in the execution, sealing up and auctioning off his real estate. The Special Court approved the request. Now, 陈克扬, claiming that the real estate in Chuansha is not owned by his father, but is his personal property, has filed an objection to the execution with the Chuansha County Government and requested a suspension of the auction. He has also filed a lawsuit against 陈耀先, demanding compensation for the guarantee of goods worth over 490 taels of silver that his father often provided.

Public Selection of Spouse for Female Residents of Women's Reformatory Scheduled; Women's Association Acts as Matchmaker, So That Single Men and Women Can Conclude a Favorable Marriage 125

The Women's Reformatory, sponsored by the Chinese Women's Temperance Association on Liuying Road in Zhabei, has been accommodating orphaned and helpless women for many years, and there is a risk of overcrowding. The association is finding it difficult to provide for clothing and food, so it plans to publicly select spouses in the near future so that single men and women can conclude favorable marriages. However, the conditions are very strict on the protection of women's rights. In addition to conducting a thorough investigation of the applicant's origin, family, occupation, temperament, and appearance, it is also stipulated that there must be a monogamous system, the age must not exceed thirty, and a security deposit of 200 yuan must be paid. If no changes occur in the middle of the relationship, the security deposit will be used to pay for the association's upbringing. If, after the marriage, it is discovered that the husband's temperament is violent and unbearable to live with, or if there are unexpected circumstances, the adopted daughter can still return to the reformatory to live, and the security deposit will be used to provide a proper life. If there are any applicants from all walks of life, they can go to the association at the end of Yuanming Road to obtain photos and fill out application documents. Then, the association will send someone to guide them to meet at the reformatory. After that, the man will be investigated and the woman's consent will be obtained, and a satisfactory marriage can be concluded on a scheduled date.

Public Security Bureau to Rectify Vegetable Markets and Shelter Beggars from Next Spring; This Year's New Life Movement Has Already Ended 129

This year's New Life Movement of the Municipal Public Security Bureau has already ended, and from next spring, it will begin to continue according to the planned plan. The details are as follows:

Work Completed: The Municipal Public Security Bureau, since its establishment this year, has stipulated a plan and followed it to promote the New Life Movement. There is only about one week left this year, and the end of the year is coming soon, so all New Life Movement work has ended. The promotion of the New Life Movement this year has been quite effective. The most outstanding achievements of the work are the training of police to familiarize them with the methods of promoting the New Life Movement, the general inspection of public places throughout the city, guiding and correcting them, and ordering them to pay attention to neatness and cleanliness, and the rectification of vendors, ordering them to set up in designated places, so as not to hinder traffic, and paying attention to hygiene. The above are the most outstanding achievements of the bureau after promoting the New Life Movement this year. After the end of this year's New Life Movement work, the New Life Movement work in the next year's plan will begin next spring. It is said that the most important points can be divided into the following points:

Pay Attention to Hygiene: Actively promote public hygiene, such as paying attention to the freshness and rot of vegetables in the city's small vegetable markets and the order of display. Other places, such as tofu shops and cold drink shops, should also be ordered to pay attention to public hygiene, so as to avoid the risk of infection from eating.

Organize the City Appearance: The city appearance is closely related to the New Life Movement, so organizing the city appearance is also one of the important tasks of the New Life Movement next year. Shops should pay attention to the neatness of their plaques and the cleanliness of the miscellaneous items displayed in front of the shop. Vendors should be actively rectified, and the display of goods at major road intersections should be prohibited. Although display is allowed on branch roads, it must be absolutely based on the principle of not hindering traffic. All such work will be the New Life Movement work planned for next year.

Beggars' Shelter: The city's beggars' shelter was opened on the 15th of this month, but the scale is larger than before. This work was originally the New Life Movement work in next year's plan, but because the weather is cold, this work has started to be carried out this year. Next year, it will continue to be carried out and will be actively accommodated, so that the beggars in the city will be free from the risk of wandering and starvation.

Ministry of Justice Orders Local Courts to Implement Prison Instruction and Education, Literacy Boards to be Hung in All Cells and Workshops, Teachers to Explain and Change Every Three Days 135

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, the Ministry of Judicial Administration yesterday ordered the local court of this city to improve the instruction and education in new and old prisons. The original text of the order is excerpted as follows: "Prison instruction and education are fundamental to improving prison administration. Education enhances the intelligence of those in prison. Neither should be neglected. To achieve fulfillment, in addition to the original instructors and teachers who should continue to be fully responsible, talent from other fields should be borrowed to make up for deficiencies. The proposed measures are as follows: (A) Regarding enriching instruction and education in new prisons: The instructor is fully responsible for the instruction of prisoners. The instructor is also responsible for paying close attention to releases from prison, punishments, and inspection of letters. The supervising authority should also send a letter to the Chinese Buddhist Association, inviting monks or lay Buddhists to take responsibility for group instruction in the new prison, and provide an appropriate subsidy to the person sent by the Buddhist Association, limited to 20 yuan per month. The results of instruction should be reported monthly by the warden of each prison, stating the facts, and submitted to the supervising officer for random inspection. Literacy boards should be hung in each cell and workshop, changed every three days, and explained by a teacher. During education, practice should be ordered, so that they can write and use [the characters]. In addition to textbooks, more books on cause and effect should be prepared, and a library should be established to arouse good thoughts. (B) Regarding enriching instruction and education in old prisons: The local county magistrate and court president or chief prosecutor should select philanthropists who are enthusiastic about public welfare or sincerely practicing monks, with the consent of the Prison Cooperation Committee members, and appoint them as prison instructors, reporting to the Provincial High Court for record. Subsidies should be negotiated within a possible range. If it is effectively managed, a report can be submitted to the High Court at the end of the year for honorary awards. Educational matters must be undertaken by prison staff themselves, with the guards assisting. Prisons where instruction and education are effectively managed will be specially rewarded by the High Court after verification."

Gangs of Beggars Forcibly Seizing Food, a Worrying Trend, Eleven Violent Individuals Detained 139

Recently, in areas such as the southern city and the inner city, there have been groups of scantily clad people, forming gangs and seeking food along the streets. Whenever they encounter pancake stalls or steamed bun shops, these individuals snatch food to fill their stomachs. The shop owners who are robbed can only resign themselves to their bad luck and not argue. These individuals, believing themselves to be successful and relying on their numbers, have become increasingly rampant. In recent days, these individuals have been seen loitering in the streets, cleverly seizing and forcibly taking food, acting without restraint. Everyone is surprised by this behavior, which is detrimental to local security. Therefore, instructions have been given to patrol officers to prohibit them at any time. The other day, a large group of emaciated young beggars, wearing ragged clothes and barefoot, snatched food in the Fangbang Road area. When the patrol officer saw them and tried to stop them, it was ineffective, and the atmosphere became tense. The officer had no choice but to call for assistance from neighboring patrols and detained eleven ringleaders, including He Jincun, Jin Nianbao, Li Yaoqing, Wang Yuxiao, Song Zuying, Chen Ziwan, Jiang Jikuan, Zhang Xinggeng, Sheng Yaoxian, Wang Zishan, and Wang Arong, taking them to the police station. The rest scattered. After a brief interrogation, the police station sent them to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau, who transferred them to the Procuratorate of the Local Court. Prosecutor Zhang Zi interrogated them and ordered them to be detained pending investigation. When the beggars were being led down from the courtroom, they smiled at each other, saying that their lives could be worry-free for the time being. Although they would have to endure the taste of iron bars, it was better than making a living in the piercing north wind all day long. The act of beggars joining together to seize food not only affects the small businesses of pancake stalls but also cultivates the habit of robbery. It is hoped that the authorities will take measures to ensure the peace and tranquility of society as soon as possible.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter Requesting Correction of Power Company's Disconnection and Orders Compensation for Losses 142

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Concession Bureau yesterday stating: "On the 20th of this month, we received a letter from Dechang Machinery Factory stating, 'Our factory's monthly electricity consumption is only about 30 yuan, and we paid a deposit of 75 taels of silver. Previously, electricity bills were collected every three months. Now, the company has changed to collecting monthly during this period of economic downturn. Our factory calculated the November electricity bill as 30 yuan and 8 cents. Because the manager was away, we notified the company that we would pay on December 16th, but we were unable to do so in time, resulting in a combined bill for November and December totaling 63 yuan and 9 cents, stating that payment was due by December 27th. If payment was not made by then, we would be notified according to regulations and given a seven-day grace period, after which the power could be cut off. However, the company did not comply with the deadline and, without exceeding the deposit of 75 taels of silver, suddenly sent someone to our factory on the morning of the 18th and immediately cut off the power line. The company not only does not sympathize with the hardships of the people and provide a grace period to users but also changed to collecting electricity fees monthly and did not notify all Shanghai users of the change in regulations or refund the excess deposits to profit from interest. This is unfair in terms of reason and principle. Our factory went to the company to negotiate on the same day and was told that the power line would be reconnected in the afternoon, and then we would be notified to recover the excess deposit and pay the electricity fee monthly thereafter. This type of user is mostly Chinese industry and commerce, which is already difficult to support in this economic downturn, and is now suffering this unexpected loss. It is unimaginable. Therefore, we specifically request your association to uphold justice and provide assistance, and send a letter to the company to prevent such unreasonable disconnections in the future, in order to assist users and warn the future,' etc. The deposit collected by the Electric Power Company from users for three months of electricity charges was originally to ensure that the company collected electricity fees every three months to prevent users from abusing electricity. Now that the company has changed to collecting electricity fees monthly, logically, the deposit paid by users should be reduced proportionally. As evidenced by the Dechang Factory incident, the arrears did not exceed the deposit, and the deadline had not exceeded the specified time in the notification. The company cut off the power line and stopped feeding electricity. Its absurd handling is already undeniable. If the deposit is reduced, the company is not unable to prevent users from abusing electricity. According to the aforementioned situation, we hereby request your bureau to order the company to return the deposit collected from users for two months of electricity fees after the company changed from annual to monthly collection, to correct the illegal disconnection of Dechang Factory, and to order compensation for the losses caused by the disconnection, in order to maintain the interests of users."

Public Concession, Health Status for November 143

The Public Concession Public Health Department chief's report for November states that the health status of the Concession during the month did not have any significant or unusual changes. Respiratory diseases did have a general increase at times, but in terms of the season, this is not at all unusual. Generally speaking, the health status of the Public Concession in November can be considered satisfactory. However, one thing that can be considered unusual is that the number of reported malaria cases in November was almost the same as the previous month, with as many as 71 reported cases of malaria during the month. This may also be due to the fact that citizens are gradually becoming accustomed to reporting diseases. However, it is difficult to speculate whether this conjecture is reliable at this time. In addition, in addition to the residents of this city, there are also northerners who were building railways in Jiangxi and contracted malaria. They returned north and passed through this port, but were too weak to continue their journey, so they stayed in Shanghai. A total of 12 of these people were sent to the Public Concession Isolation Hospital, and 9 of them died soon after. The Concession health authorities have now agreed on a method of cooperation with the Chinese side to avoid the spread of malignant malaria everywhere. Furthermore, most of the above 11 people also suffered from dysentery at the same time, one suffered from typhoid fever, and one suffered from eczema, making treatment hopeless, resulting in death. A total of four cases of smallpox were reported this month, two Chinese and two Westerners. A total of 89 people were bitten by rabid dogs and requested treatment this month, 18 of whom came from other ports. The birth rate of Chinese and foreign residents in this port: a total of 92 foreign births were reported, 81 of whom lived in the Concession, divided into 38 boys and 43 girls. The number of Chinese children born and reported increased by about 400 from the same month last year, totaling 2,137, of whom 2,059 lived in the Concession, divided into 1,163 baby boys and 896 baby girls. In terms of deaths, there were a total of 31 foreigners, of which 68% were non-Chinese Asians. The major causes of death were pulmonary tuberculosis, heart disease, inflammation, and digestive system diseases. Among the Chinese, the major causes of death were old age, pulmonary tuberculosis, typhoid fever, and bronchitis.

Zhuanqiao, Civil Education Center Improves Ancestor Worship Methods 147

The Zhuanqiao Public Education Center in Shanghai County, in order to improve folk ancestor worship, has drafted improvement measures and decided to implement them starting in the 25th year of the Republic of China. A copy has been submitted to the county government and county education bureau for record. The following is a summary of the measures: These measures will be implemented in the Tongqiao basic education area of this center. All households participating before implementation must take an oath. The implementation of these measures will be supervised by the executive committee member of the Tongqiao Township Improvement Association. The day before Qingming, Summer Solstice, Zhongyuan, and Winter Solstice each year is designated as Ancestor Remembrance Day. All households in this area who worship their ancestors must do so on this day. On Ancestor Remembrance Day, each family should clean the interior and exterior of the house and set up a table in the hall with four dishes of seasonal local vegetables. The head of the household should lead the family in bowing three times, and the head of the household should talk about the good deeds of the ancestors, or invite someone to give a speech. On Ancestor Remembrance Day, relatives and friends must not exchange greetings. Burning of ingot silk and ghost money is not allowed, and crying for the ancestors is not allowed. On Ancestor Remembrance Day, supervisors will conduct random checks. Households that have recently lost a member may make appropriate changes.

Liao Aqian Dies Tragically from Coal Poisoning 150

Liao Aqian, a 61-year-old man from Chaozhou, had retired in Shanghai due to old age. He was lodging on a bed in the Qiacheng Food Store, owned by a fellow townsman, at 25 Rue Pessonnel in the French Concession, working as a street vendor from early morning until night. On the 21st, at 2 PM, Liao suddenly felt cold and unwell. Having no place to rest in the Qiacheng store during the day, he shivered restlessly. At that time, Gu Benlin (37 years old), a cook from Pudong working at the store, whose residence was in the overhanging building at 37 Yinhe Lane, Min'guo Road, saw Liao's discomfort and kindly invited him to rest at his home. He accompanied Liao there and, due to the cold weather, lit a coal briquette stove and placed it beside the bed for warmth. Unexpectedly, Liao was poisoned by the coal fumes. At 4 PM, Gu went to check on him and found that Liao, due to his old age and weakened state, was unable to resist. His breathing was faint. Gu immediately called for an ambulance and a doctor, who performed artificial respiration for two hours without success. At 6 PM, Liao was rushed to Guangci Hospital, but it was too late; he died. The French police were notified and sent detectives to investigate. Meanwhile, the body was taken to the Tongren Zhuan'yuan Funeral Hall for examination. The deceased had a son named Jin, currently 26 years old, working as a partner at the Jincheng Pawnshop at 113 Tongzhou Road in Hongkou. Detectives were sent to inform him. The case will be reported to the Second Special District Court today for examination.

Hunan Provincial Highway Bureau to Install German-Style Gas Generators 153

According to the Central News Agency, the highway system in Hunan Province has developed rapidly in recent years. The Highway Bureau, due to business expansion and increased routes, feels that the number of vehicles is insufficient for its application, therefore, it has specially ordered sixty "Wanguo" brand automobiles from Shanghai. The first batch of twenty vehicles has already arrived. The authorities, considering the excessive consumption of gasoline, are planning to convert to gas generators. The Finance and Construction Departments' Audit Committee and the Highway Bureau each sent representatives to form a Gas Generator Review Committee, which held a technical competition on Tanbao Road. Competitors included Li Baohe's Chinese Gas Engine Manufacturing Factory from Hankou, the Xiangde type from the Shanghai Chinese Gas Vehicle Manufacturing Company, and the Tang Zhongmin type from the Shanghai Zhongming Factory. After a month-long evaluation, the Xiangde type was deemed the best, followed by the Li Baohe type, and then the Tang Zhongmin type. The committee reported this to the Construction Department, and it is reported that the Construction Department has also decided to adopt the Xiangde type gas generator across the board. A contract is expected to be signed soon, and the conversion to gas generators will be implemented in the near future for use on various routes.

Shanghai Hunting Association Schedules a Major Hunt in Yushan 156

Yushan is located on the border of Zhejiang and Jiangxi, connecting to Xia. The high mountains and steep ridges form a natural hunting area abundant with tigers, leopards, muntjacs, wild boars, and other beasts. The Shanghai Hunting Association had long designated it as a major hunting area. However, for several years, the area had been disturbed by Communist bandits, who plundered people's belongings, causing unease day and night. Therefore, despite their courage, they dared not attempt a hunt. Recently, after President Chiang Kai-shek suppressed the remaining bandits and the local area was pacified, Zhang Yinxun, a prominent member of the association from Yushan, also returned to his hometown to rebuild his home. He found that the number of wild animals in the mountains and fields had increased significantly compared to before. He sent a letter to Liu Jiuwei and Yuan Yang'an, executives of the Shanghai Hunting Association, inviting them to organize an expedition. The timing coincided with the Shanghai Hunting Association's major hunting period. The executives sent a general notice to hunters from all sides, including Qian Hongliang from Qianjiang, Weng Wenyin from Hangzhou, Chen Anyu, Yu Jixian, Shen Tu Chen from Tonglu, as well as local comrades Zhang Yuan, Heng Fang, Heng Quan, Li Liangmei, Yi Zhenchang, and He Jingdi. Registration is at 431, 4th Floor, Continental Emporium.

Request for Flexible Measures Regarding the Movement of Dinghua Sulfur, etc. 157

The National New Pharmaceutical Industry Association yesterday submitted a petition to the Ministries of Finance, Industry, and Military Affairs, stating that Dinghua sulfur is finely textured, different from ordinary sulfur. It meets the standards specified in the Chinese Pharmacopoeia, making it a pure medicinal product. It is commonly used in the treatment of diseases, both internally and externally, and is sold by pharmaceutical merchants in very small quantities. However, it is currently prohibited from being transported and sold at will due to its use in the production of gunpowder. In reality, with the advancement of modern science, sulfur is no longer widely used for making gunpowder. Although potassium chlorate has explosive properties, it is also a necessary medicine for treating throat inflammation and other ailments. The regulations of the Salt and Sulfur Bureau require large-scale purchases for transportation and sales, such as a minimum purchase of 2,000 pounds of sulfur at a time. Although transportation permits can be issued, the need for such a large quantity is non-existent for medicinal purposes. Therefore, although there is a way to obtain a permit, there is no need to obtain a permit for such a large quantity. As for small-scale purchases, there is absolutely no way to obtain them. In fact, if the goal is to prevent the private manufacture of military firearms, the focus should be on restricting large-scale purchases. If small quantities of one, two, or three to five pounds are needed for medicinal purposes but cannot be purchased, wouldn't this be the opposite of the government's intention to prevent private manufacturing? Therefore, the Association has decided to request the relevant ministries to negotiate a method for the small-scale transportation and sale of Dinghua sulfur, potassium chlorate, and potassium nitrate for medicinal purposes, in order to facilitate business and benefit medical treatment.

The residents of Lutongkang Lane near the Sacred Heart Convent, collectively signed and sealed a letter proving that Cao Mao, wife of the husband's mother was being abused by her husband, but was falsely reported to the police by the husband's mother, Cao Chengyao, claiming that the wife had injured her parents. The case has been brought to court. They request that justice be served. After sending Wu Guowei to investigate and confirm that the charges were indeed false, it was resolved: To send a letter to the Women's Association, to send a letter to the Legal Department of the French police, to appoint a lawyer to appear in court for the trial, and to request lawyers Wang Shizong and Huang Zengjie Yangwu to serve as advocates. C. The French Water and Electricity Company is increasing the deposit for tap water meters. At a time when the market is depressed and business is sluggish, citizens cannot afford unexpected burdens. Moreover, the deposit system has been in place for a long time without causing harm. There is no need to increase it. It was resolved: To write to the Water Company to strongly argue for the cancellation of the proposed increase, taking into account the livelihood of the citizens.

The Wei Ya Restaurant Trademark Case 160

The Wei Ya Restaurant in this city is famous for its exquisite Cantonese cuisine. It was founded in the late Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty on Chongming Road in Hongkou. The manager, He Yuechi, has always been praised by people from all walks of life for his excellent cooking skills. Later, the building was renovated, and the main restaurant was relocated to the intersection of North Sichuan Road and Peng Road, with a branch on Sima Road. These are the only two locations. He registered his business name separately with the Industry and Commerce Registration Bureau. However, in recent months, a counterfeit Wei Ya Restaurant and Wei Ya Restaurant have been established in the Baliqiao Road area. The owner believes that these counterfeit restaurants threaten the reputation of the real Wei Ya, and sent separate letters to the owners of the counterfeit restaurants, demanding that they cease using the Wei Ya name. The owner of the counterfeit Wei Ya Restaurant acknowledged the unfairness of their actions and immediately changed their name. However, the Wei Ya Restaurant owner refused to comply. The real Wei Ya Restaurant filed a lawsuit with the Second Special District Court, requesting that the counterfeit restaurant be prohibited from using the Wei Ya name and be required to pay damages. The court issued a summons. The other day, He Yuechi, accompanied by his lawyer, He Qingyun, appeared in court. After questioning by Judge Li Liang, the defendant admitted to using the Wei Ya name without permission and agreed to change the name. A settlement was reached in court. The defendant will change the name of Wei Ya to Xu Ya within one week. If the defendant fails to comply within the deadline, they will be required to pay the plaintiff a daily loss of 20 yuan, starting from the date of the unauthorized use of the name. The plaintiff will be entitled to request and enforce the payment.

Qing Ping Yuan Restaurant Expands Business 161

The Qing Ping Yuan Restaurant on Xixinqiao Street, east of the Great World, has been open for more than 30 years and is one of the leading Beijing cuisine restaurants in the city. Improving Chinese Accounting Forms: Reducing Costs and Guiding Usage 162

In recent years, many businesses have been paying attention to improving accounting practices and adopting the improved Chinese accounting system developed by accountant Xu Yongzuo. This improved Chinese accounting system, after being registered with the Ministry of Interior of the National Government in 1933, has been manufactured and sold by the Standard Account Book and Form Manufacturing and Sales Office. Purchasers have found it very convenient, as they can refer to the "Introduction to Improved Chinese Accounting." Recently, accountant Xu has also compiled a book titled "Examples of Improved Chinese Accounting," which provides specific account formats for various account book entries, postings, and closings, printed as a book. Its contents are clearly organized, consistent from beginning to end, and resemble the account books and forms actually used by various industries and businesses. Those who adopt the improved accounting system will find it easier to understand its usage. The Standard Account Book and Form Manufacturing and Sales Office, recognizing the increasing number of adopters, has prepared a large stock of new products to meet the needs of various industries at the beginning of the New Year. The paper, printing, and binding are even better, and the cost has been reduced somewhat due to the use of mass production methods. Therefore, the selling price has also been slightly reduced compared to before. New Year's gifts related to improved Chinese accounting are also being given to those who purchase account books and forms, allowing them to refer to them at any time. In the past month, many companies and firms have pre-ordered new books or specially printed new books, and they have now been successively delivered. According to reporter investigations, accountant Xu has been working very hard on the improved Chinese accounting movement in recent years. The Standard Account Book and Form Manufacturing and Sales Office, which distributes improved Chinese account books and forms, has also made significant improvements to its production methods. This is indeed good news for the industrial and commercial circles of our country. The following are the improved features of the account books and forms and the New Year's preferential measures:

Improved Features of Account Books and Forms: According to accountant Xu, there are ten special features of improved Chinese account books and forms: Each account book has a fixed format printed on it, with clear divisions for the item to be recorded, the amount, the date, and the page number for cross-referencing. This makes recording and reviewing very convenient. There are many kinds of account books with separate spaces for recording amounts, with the amount columns divided into places for recording amounts in a more organized way. The end of each account book provides detailed instructions on how to use it, based on the format of that account book. The bookkeeper can follow these instructions. At the end of each account book, there are 32 bookkeeping instructions, specifying opening, recording, posting, settlement, and other procedures, so that the bookkeeper has a certain set of rules to follow. The beginning of each account book includes a list of managing personnel, which should include the name of the account book, the name of the bookkeeper, and the date of handover before bookkeeping can begin. This clarifies the responsibilities of the bookkeeper. Each account book is numbered page by page using a numbering machine to prevent missing or torn pages. The numbers can also be noted during posting for easy review. There are many types of account book formats, from primary books to subsidiary books, totaling ten types of paper. The formats required by various industries are complete. There are also a dozen types of accounts and vouchers, and the accounts required for settlement are all complete. Vouchers used for signing off on receipts and payments and for transmitting accounting information, whether for cash or transfers, are also available. The paper used is all domestic goods, with Luo Di paper used for various copying books and Hai Yue paper and Mao Bian paper used for journals. They are finely printed and bound in cloth, making them attractive and durable. Manufacturing is done using scientific methods and mass production, so delivery is fast and the selling price is lower than that of ordinary account books. There are books such as "Introduction to Improved Chinese Accounting" and "Examples of Improved Chinese Accounting" to provide detailed explanations of accounting principles and methods, as well as concrete examples. There is also a service department set up within the accountant Xu's office to provide services to users at any time. Anyone who adopts the improved Chinese accounting system can consult with the department at any time if they have any questions. They are always happy to provide guidance.

New Year's Preferential Treatment for Users: According to a key employee of the Standard Account Book and Form Manufacturing and Sales Office, the selling price has already been reduced due to mass production, which is already a preferential treatment for users. However, it is feared that adopters may not be fully aware of the accounting principles and methods. Therefore, they have agreed with accountant Xu to include books related to improved Chinese accounting as gifts. Anyone who purchases account books and forms totaling 5 yuan will receive a copy of "Introduction to Improved Chinese Accounting". Those who purchase account books and forms totaling 10 yuan will receive two copies of "Introduction to Improved Chinese Accounting" and "Examples of Improved Chinese Accounting". Those who purchase account books and forms totaling 15 yuan will receive three copies of "Introduction to Improved Chinese Accounting," "Examples of Improved Chinese Accounting," and "Collected Essays on Improved Chinese Accounting". These books are all written for improved Chinese accounting. The "Examples" book alone has a total of 750 pages and concretely displays account books with their postings, trial balances, and closings. It shows all the various formats, and is a very practical book. However, this gift offer is limited to the next two months. Anyone who purchases account books and forms from the general distribution office at 123 Aidaoya Road on the third floor, or from authorized distributors such as the Scientific Instrument Museum, World Bookstore, Yuanyi Printing House, Qiatat Paper Store, or Gaoshengda Paper Store, will also receive the gifts. If users need the Manufacturing and Sales Office to design an account book organization or specify the types of account books to be matched, the Office will be happy to provide such service.

A Letter to Students of Beiping Schools from the Principal of a Jiangsu Province Middle School 167

The Jiangsu Provincial United Association of Secondary Schools yesterday sent a letter to the students of various schools in Beiping, which read: "To the students of all schools in Beiping, greetings. Recent newspaper reports have revealed your magnificent movements for the sake of national territorial integrity and sovereign independence. You have not feared knives and axes or brute force. This spirit of indomitable power is truly the lifeblood of the nation and the glory of national revival. We, located far away in Jiangnan, upon hearing of this, cannot help but feel inspired by the righteousness of your determined movement and admire your fortitude. However, the national crisis is not yet over, and wolves are at our side. The peace of the entire nation cannot be hoped for overnight. The task of saving the nation and seeking survival in the future rests upon our shoulders. We must share the same hatred against the enemy, endure what must be endured, and speak out when we must speak out. If we do not slacken in this resolve, we will surely succeed in the end. While demonstrations and marches can arouse people's hearts for a time, they are not the key to saving the nation and seeking survival. Your spirit has already been displayed in this determined movement. May you continue this spirit and take a further step to dedicate yourselves to the country. We believe that because the national populace lacks education and has a shallow understanding of the nation, righteousness has waned, and selfishness abounds, leading to the emergence of traitors, which is heartbreaking to say. We have several points of self-encouragement to share with you, hoping you will adopt them:

1. Cultivate the spirit of avenging humiliation and the idea that adversity strengthens a nation. Those who are in distress should know their responsibility for the rise and fall of the nation. We must have the determination of Goujian to destroy Wu, and we must strive for advancement. Not avenging hatred or wiping away humiliation is a disgrace for a scholar. Without composure and fortitude, one cannot shoulder great responsibilities. Today's enemy may be strong, and we may be weak, but we must not be afraid. If all of us are willing to be like Tian Heng's loyal retainers, then even the might of Qin cannot do anything to us. We should be wary of the cunning of traitors. We should first demand excellence from ourselves and then extend it to others. How can we allow ourselves to be at the mercy of others forever?

2. Strengthen our physical fitness. A difficult task cannot be accomplished by relying on extraordinary people. National crises cannot be resolved overnight. In the future, we will need to work tirelessly. Without strong physical fitness, how can we maintain a persevering spirit? The scholarly habit of weakness has been around for a long time. We should learn from past mistakes and recognize that physical training is more important than all other forms of self-cultivation. We should encourage each other to create a national atmosphere of valuing martial arts. Do not think that this is a roundabout way when disaster is imminent. We must know that the places where we will shed blood and sacrifice ourselves are not just one place or one time.

3. Engage in extensive work to train the populace. The foundation of the nation lies in the people. Without a strong organization of the people, the nation cannot prosper. Everyone knows this. China has endured thousands of years of autocratic rule. The people only know how to be obedient and regard national affairs as the responsibility of the government. Therefore, how can we rely solely on the government to shoulder the task of saving the nation and seeking survival and resist strong enemies? To understand shame and teach warfare, one must be able to fight for oneself. If the organization of the populace can achieve this, then even if the enemy has strong troops pressing the border, what do we have to fear? Therefore, our efforts to save the nation and seek survival are not without active work. In the future, we should go deep into the grassroots, engage in training and organizing the people, and create a strong foundation for the people. This can not only resist foreign aggression and seek survival but also make traitors disappear. If we move in a unified direction, we can advance on multiple fronts, training and organizing the people of one village in one village, and training and organizing the people of one county in one county. After ten years of growth and training, what do we have to fear that the nation will not prosper? We, the undersigned, encourage ourselves with this principle and also lead tens of thousands of young people in Jiangnan to strive for this goal. As long as we have one breath left, we will surely seek the revival of the Chinese nation and wash away the deep shame. We offer our sincere thoughts, hoping for your consideration. We remain, the Jiangsu Provincial United Association of Secondary Schools, respectfully."
