Director Pan Gave a Speech Yesterday at the Short-Term Elementary Education Research Conference, Explaining the Urgency of Short-Term Elementary Schools in China's Current Situation and Hoping that All Teachers Will Integrate Their Profession and Career 170

The Short-Term Elementary Education Research Conference of this city held its second general meeting at Shangwen Elementary School at 2 PM yesterday. More than 80 representatives from various schools attended. Zhang Zeng'an chaired the meeting, and Huang Fengming recorded the minutes. Regarding the results of various studies, representatives from Wan Zhu, Shangwen, He'an, Meixi, and Xicheng schools were recommended, and Wan Zhu was recommended as the convener. The conference chairman was given a deadline of January 15th to submit the research results to the Education Bureau. Afterwards, Director Pan of the Education Bureau gave a speech, the main points of which are as follows:

"Gentlemen, today's meeting of the Short-Term Elementary Education Research Conference is taking place, and I have a few words to say to you briefly. The national compulsory education, as stipulated in China, is six years. One should receive six years of education, and if it is absolutely necessary, one should also receive four years of education. However, due to the financial difficulties of the country and the large number of out-of-school children, if we strictly follow the six-year or four-year system, the government may have difficulty raising funds for a while, and it will take a long time for most children to receive education, and we don't know how many years we will have to wait. But when national disasters become serious, we want to get many out-of-school children educated in the shortest time possible, and we must shorten the time limit. Therefore, the Ministry of Education stipulates this temporary emergency measure, which is not a regular method. This is what we should first recognize clearly. Don't think that one year of short-term elementary school is enough. This is the first point.

The second point to make clear is that the one-year short-term elementary school allows out-of-school children to be educated in shifts in a very short period. For example, with the four-year system, a school that can accommodate 200 people can only graduate 200 people in four years. However, with the short-term elementary school system, the same school can teach 200 people every year. Although we cannot make such an accurate calculation, we can at least guarantee that it will double. Therefore, the Ministry of Education stipulates this method, which can allow out-of-school children to receive a superficial education in rotation in the shortest period. The third point is that some people say that the short-term elementary school has too short a time limit and too little teaching material, which is not enough to meet the needs. Indeed, but we don't have to worry about this. One is better than none. Although one year of education is short, it is better than no education at all. Second, we want to make it possible for them to seek further education. Because they can still enter community schools, tutoring schools, or other social education opportunities when they grow up. With this one year of foundation, they can gradually improve in the future. Therefore, short-term elementary school is to give them some tools so that they will have the opportunity to receive further education in the future.

In short, short-term elementary school is to adapt to the current situation that the country is very poor and there are so many out-of-school children. Therefore, there is this flexible method. Then, since short-term elementary school is so necessary, how should we, who are short-term elementary school teachers, do our work? Therefore, everyone is here today to research and discuss, solve difficulties, and seek the progress of teaching effectiveness. However, I can tell you my personal thoughts.

I think that taking on this kind of position is really the country's expectation of you, which is not enough, and the career is important, so this short-term elementary school is set up. Therefore, you must serve under this principle, even if the work is more and the reward is less, and you cannot distinguish the level of teachers. It can be said that your spirit of service to the country and society is better than theirs. Therefore, I hope that everyone will do their best, and the spirit of service must be full, so that you can truly work for the country and society. Second, teaching students in short-term elementary schools is different from ordinary elementary schools. Ordinary elementary schools stipulate age of admission, which is quite neat, and the levels are also very similar. In short-term elementary schools, the ages vary, and the levels are uneven. It is worth noting what methods to use to teach them in the same class and achieve the same results within a certain period. Therefore, special research should be conducted on short-term elementary education for this reason. Third, it is more difficult to be a teacher in a short-term elementary school. For example, recruiting students is more difficult than in ordinary elementary schools. Because the Education Bureau first investigates the number of children in each district who cannot enter ordinary elementary schools, and then distributes short-term elementary schools in each district. Teachers in short-term elementary schools must recruit these children who are unable or have no time to enter ordinary elementary schools, which is the real meaning of running short-term elementary schools. It would be wrong to recruit students who are already studying in ordinary elementary schools. Everyone should pay attention to this point. Therefore, teachers who work in short-term elementary schools must have enthusiasm for the country, society, and children, and a spirit of willingness to sacrifice. Teachers should regard half of their work as a profession and half as a career. Profession and career are different. Profession is to mechanically seek material life, while career is spiritual life. Everyone should integrate profession and career, recognizing that this work is not only a profession for seeking life but also the most noble career for the country and society."

Economic Supplement

American Monetary Policy and the Anglo-American Currency War 198

— Sen Yu

———Chinese Currency in a Vice———

Following China's new monetary policy, another significant event has occurred in the world's financial markets in recent days: the sudden and severe drop in silver prices on the London silver market due to the United States' cessation of silver purchases. The market situation became extremely unstable, and trading was even suspended on the tenth of this month, causing an unprecedented disruption since the European War of 1914. Although the United States is still purchasing silver in London, easing concerns somewhat, the market price continues to fall due to the significant difference between the amounts sold and purchased.

A Review of American Silver Policy and its Factors

The initial manifestation of American silver policy was the so-called Thomas Amendment in Part 3 of the Emergency Agricultural Relief and Currency Inflation Act of May 1933. This amendment authorized the President to change the silver dollar's quantity, freely mint coins, adopt a bimetallic system, and receive war debt principal and interest with silver up to a limit of 200 million yuan (but only received 10 million yuan from the UK). Subsequently, there was the London Silver Agreement of July 1933, which was approved in December, followed by the promulgation of the Domestic Silver Purchase Act. The Bitman Amendment in the Gold Reserve Act of January 1934, the Silver Purchase Act of June, and the Silver Nationalization Order of August followed. Among these, the Silver Purchase Act of June 1934 was the most important. It stipulated that currency reserves should be 75% gold and 25% silver, aiming to achieve this ratio by purchasing silver domestically and internationally. It also authorized the Secretary of the Treasury to issue silver certificates and empowered the President to order silver to be deposited into the mint, regardless of the owner or location.

The United States' active approach to silver was naturally based on the interests of domestic silver-producing states and the desire to indirectly promote currency inflation. However, focusing solely on domestic reasons is clearly insufficient. In reality, the interests of silver mine owners are not necessarily the most important aspect of the policy. From June 1934 to July of this year, the government purchased 472.2 million ounces of silver in thirteen months. Of this, only 26 million ounces were newly produced domestically, and the remaining 112.2 million ounces purchased from the public were mostly imported from overseas. This shows that the benefits gained by domestic mine owners were not as significant as claimed. To study American silver policy, we should extend it to the international relationship, but if we simply explain it as "increasing the purchasing power of silver-using countries," that is still insufficient. In addition to aiming to increase the consumption capacity of South American and Far Eastern countries by raising silver prices to develop its trade, the United States also attempts to control the currency rights of the above-mentioned countries that use silver standard and gold exchange standard, especially China, to expand the dollar bloc. In summary, silver policy is also a weapon in international financial struggles, and its conflict with the United Kingdom is particularly fierce.

Furthermore, we must also discuss the international gold-silver bimetallic system. Recently, there has been a high demand for adopting a bimetallic system, especially from the United States. The motivation for the Americans to advocate for the bimetallic system, in addition to the general theoretical basis of the so-called equilibratory action, is mainly related to the special relationship with silver. The United States not only holds a significant amount of silver itself, but American capital also controls more than 60% of the world's annual silver production. Therefore, restoring silver as a currency and fundamentally resolving its outlet is the most appropriate thing to do. The United States already has a lot of gold, and if it accumulates more silver at the same time, it will control most of the world's gold and silver, allowing it to monopolize resources. In addition to the country, it can also force all countries to uniformly implement a gold-silver bimetallic system, and under the name of the international bimetallic system, manipulate international finance.

The main objectives of American silver policy are listed below:

The Failure of Silver Policy and its New Trends

Given the above objectives of American silver policy, what are the results? Undeniably, apart from the silver mine owners who have indeed profited domestically, the majority of the people still do not benefit. Internationally, the realization of the bimetallic system is still slim. The purchasing power of silver-using countries has not only failed to increase, but has instead deepened their level of panic, causing the purchasing power to shrink even further. China, Mexico, Peru, etc., have suffered the most. Moreover, this has created opportunities for the United Kingdom to expand the gold-pound group's activities.

Based on the above failures, the United States has to reconsider its silver policy to a considerable extent. However, it is difficult to find a solution. It is in a difficult position. Continuing as before is not allowed by the facts, and suddenly abandoning it is neither desirable nor possible. Therefore, the United States has been uneasy in recent months.

However, as of now, the situation has become increasingly tight. In early November, China was forced to change its currency system and announce a new monetary policy due to the urgency of financial panic. In addition, the United Kingdom's activities in the international financial market have been very active recently, which has forced the United States to take necessary countermeasures.

The American strategy finally emerged a few days ago, which is the current change in the London silver market. When the change suddenly occurred, the reasons spread by all parties were complex and confusing, and no one could agree. Some said that the United States intended to purchase silver at a low price to reduce the amount it paid; some said that the amount of silver dumped was too large, and the United States could not absorb it for a while; some said that European cash no longer flows to the United States in large quantities, making the United States unwilling to purchase silver at a high price; some said that a large amount of Chinese silver was smuggled to Japan, and the United States had to come out and crack down on it, etc. These do have considerable relevance, and the last two are undeniable facts. However, these alone are not enough to explain and cannot be considered the main factors of the silver change. We must also pay attention to the unfolding of a new stage of the Anglo-American currency war. (Details below)

As for some people's speculation that this is the prelude to the United States' abandonment of silver policy, I don't think that's necessarily the case. Based on the following points, the United States may not abandon silver: The United States has huge investments in silver mines at home and abroad. If the silver issue is abandoned, it is impossible in practice. The U.S. government has purchased a lot of silver in the past ten months or so. If the silver policy is abandoned halfway, how will these stored silver be disposed of? Silver is still a weapon in the international financial war. If the United States wants to win the world's economic stage, it must still use it. The United States' plan for the international bimetallic system has not been interrupted, and silver is the protagonist of the bimetallic system. If it is negative about silver, the realization of the bimetallic system will be even more hopeless.

Therefore, I think that the United States will probably not abandon its silver policy. The problem is just how to implement it. As for the price of silver, unless absolutely necessary, it may not fall indefinitely, because according to the above points, the excessive drop in silver prices has more disadvantages than advantages for the United States itself. Based on recent facts, the future strategy of the United States on silver policy can be roughly speculated as follows: Transfer the center of the international silver market from London to New York to combat the United Kingdom and allow the United States to further manipulate the world's silver. This point has been explained by Finance Minister Morgenthau. Purchase silver directly from the Far East and other places, so as to directly place the finance of those places in the hands of the United States. Make every effort to prevent China from leaving silver, and further encircle China's currency into the dollar bloc. Exchange goods for silver, so that it can directly obtain silver without spending gold, and also promote the sale of surplus products. Representative Thais, a silver faction activist, has reportedly made this claim.

The future success or failure of the above points is another issue. In short, they are roughly the trend of American silver policy in the future. Among them, the most obvious manifestation is the currency challenge against the United Kingdom, and the Anglo-American currency war is nothing more than the fuse of this silver change. This can be a very important proof from the remarks of U.S. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau and the remarks of silver faction members such as Thomas Pittman. But here we must also mention China's currency problem. Unfortunately, China's currency is now the target of the new struggle between the dollar and the pound. It is undeniable that the recent currency reform has objectively strengthened the confrontation between the United States and the United Kingdom and launched the new currency war between the two major groups of the dollar and the pound.

(3) The confrontation between the Dollar Bloc and the Pound Bloc

To understand the current situation of the dollar-pound war, we must first understand the lineup of their groups and the situation of past struggles.

Currency is a weapon in the era of financial capitalism to compete for markets. The currency group is a natural product of economic groups, and its combination is more important than general economic groups. Either based solely on the commonality of currency; or based on the common interdependence of currency, that is, taking the mutual dependence of the external value of currency as a link, with the economically superior country exercising economic and even political dominance. The former is like the gold group led by France; the latter is like the pound bloc centered on the United Kingdom and the dollar bloc centered on the United States.

In the current world, only these three can be called huge currency groups. Although Japan is combining with the puppet Manchuria to carry out its Far East currency group, its financial power is still too lacking, and it cannot be global. Even among the above three groups, the gold group can only maintain its "not yet collapsed" state. It is currently in turmoil, and its power is weakening day by day. The position of the franc is also precarious, and its future is unpredictable. Therefore, the most intense competition in the world is only between the dollar and the pound groups. The dollar bloc is led by the United States and includes Mexico, Guatemala, Honduras, El Salvador, Nicaragua, Panama, Costa Rica in Central America, Cuba, Haiti, Santo Domingo in the West Indies, Venezuela, Colombia, Peru, Ecuador, Bolivia, Brazil, Chile, and the Philippines in South America. The pound bloc is led by the United Kingdom and includes the self-governing colonies and territories of the empire, as well as Sweden, Norway, Denmark, Finland, Portugal, Argentina, etc. Although Canada is a British territory, its economic relationship with the United States is particularly close. In 1933, it also followed the United States in devaluing its currency. Some people also include it in the dollar bloc; but the United Kingdom is now trying its best to tighten this ring, using the activities of the Imperial Central Bank to strengthen the relationship between the United Kingdom and Canada and resist the power of the United States. This can also be said to be the target of the dollar and pound blocs' competition.

(4) The War Between the Dollar and the Pound

The history of the international currency war is not short. The specific beginning of the war was the United Kingdom's prohibition of gold exports and abandonment of the gold standard in October 1931. After the gold standard was abandoned, the pound fell sharply. With the stimulus of the exchange rate, the United Kingdom's foreign trade suddenly took the advantage, not only overwhelming European countries, but also encroaching on the commodity markets of Japan and the United States. Then, Japan also abandoned the gold standard. In April 1933, the United States also officially announced the cessation of cash payments, withdrew from the gold standard, and implemented currency devaluation to fight against the United Kingdom and Japan. The struggle between the United States and the pound is even more profound. In the summer of 1933, the London World Economic Conference ended in a breakdown mainly because the United States was unwilling to stabilize exchange rates, and the confrontation between the United States and the United Kingdom was irreconcilable. Since then, the two countries' struggle for currency hegemony has not stopped. On the one hand, they use huge equalization funds to dump exchange rates; on the other hand, they form huge groups and seize the world's financial territory. The United States has not only purchased a large amount of gold from the world, but also formulated the above-mentioned silver policy, announced the Silver Purchase Act, and actively purchased silver.

As mentioned earlier, the United States implemented the silver policy mainly to manipulate the world's silver market and use it as a weapon for international financial struggle, except for a small part based on its domestic motives. It also uses this to control the currencies of countries that use the gold exchange standard and the silver standard, so as to expand the sphere of influence of the dollar bloc. Among them, seizing China's currency is the most important goal; if China's currency joins the dollar bloc, this huge market will not be difficult for the United States to manipulate.

(5) The Anglo-American Currency War in China

The United States' ambition for China's currency rights has been expressed for a long time. The Kemmerer Plan in 1930 was prepared to directly link China's currency unit with the U.S. dollar in order to develop American trade and investment in China; however, this plan was not realized due to various reasons.

After the offensive silver policy was adopted, unfortunately, it caused too much financial panic in China and led to China's discontent. At that time, it was advantageous to the United Kingdom. On the one hand, the United Kingdom secretly carried out planned sabotage, and on the other hand, it pleased China on the surface. It also planned to encircle China's currency into the pound bloc, and China's currency unit followed the pound. At that time, the demand for China to join the pound bloc had begun to rise very high. In order to consider China's trend towards extremism, the United States had to slightly ease its silver purchase procedures.

However, at the beginning of last month, China finally implemented a new monetary policy. Although this policy is not formally joining the pound bloc, it is at least quite beneficial to the United Kingdom. On the American side, it did not generate a good impression. On the contrary, due to the United Kingdom's activity, it clearly expressed displeasure. Therefore, the two countries' currency struggle in China has intensified dramatically in secret.

This time, the United States' reduction of silver purchases in London can also be mainly said to be a manifestation of the beginning of a new stage of the Anglo-American struggle, with China's currency as the target. The leader of the silver faction, Thomas, publicly attacked the United Kingdom, accusing the United Kingdom of absorbing Chinese currency to expand the pound bloc, and clearly stated that the pound bloc is an organization to counter the United States. The United States had to rise up to deal with it. In addition to launching a frontal attack on the United Kingdom, it is also a demonstration by the United States to China; the United States may use the destruction of the Chinese financial market as a threat to directly negotiate with China, demanding a change in the current monetary policy to benefit the United States, and at least to exclude British activities. This development is not impossible; if the Anglo-American struggle in China really reaches a boiling point and triggers a more serious financial storm, the sacrifices made by China in the clamp are really terrible. We cannot absolutely trust excessive optimism, thinking that China's current financial situation is quite stable, and the foreign exchange rate is also stable, and it has the power to break the onslaught of the tide. In essence, although China's currency system has nominally lifted the shackles of silver, it cannot completely get rid of silver after all; China's international payments still have to be calculated in silver. In peacetime, China can stabilize international exchange rates by the unlimited purchase and sale of foreign exchange by the three major banks; however, the fund for trading foreign exchange has not yet been independent from silver. If the silver market changes, it will directly affect the amount of China's stable exchange rate fund. The foreign exchange market situation in the past few days has already revealed the difficulty of maintaining it, and the most severe days are yesterday (20th) and today (21st), and its future is still unpredictable. Some say that the United Kingdom can assist China, and yesterday (20th), HSBC sold long-term contracts, which seems to have the meaning of maintaining foreign exchange; but can the United Kingdom really work hard for China? In fact, it is not just to maintain its own interests! To put it bluntly, it is just using China's currency as a tool to resist the dollar! What good will it ultimately do for China?

Naturally, on the other hand, we may be able to find a temporary compromise point between the United States and the United Kingdom; that is, when the struggle between the two sides develops to a certain stage, there may be a temporary truce (but it is only temporary). Based on the United Kingdom's current situation, it may reconcile with the United States, be willing to negotiate with the United States, sign an agreement on economic interests in China, or obtain the United States' cessation of offensive with other exchange conditions (such as Anglo-American cooperation in the naval conference, etc.). At the same time, it seems that the United States may not necessarily be tough to the end. If the entire Chinese market is too chaotic, it will also be detrimental to American trade and investment; and the dramatic changes in silver prices, as mentioned above, will also have adverse effects on its domestic situation; in addition, it often harms Central and South American countries, which is indirectly harming the United States. Therefore, if it can obtain certain concessions from the United Kingdom, it is not impossible to compromise. However, who will be the main sacrificial object of this compromise?

The Current State of Shandong Fisheries and its Improvement (Continued) 199

— Ding Fengbai

The Fisheries of Qingdao, Shandong Under Japanese Control

The encroachment of Japanese fishing power into Shandong is not a recent phenomenon. More than a decade ago, the Japanese presence in Shandong's fishing industry was already exceptionally large. The two major fish-producing areas of Shandong – Weihaiwei and Qingdao – were already under Japanese control and manipulation. The main reason for this was that the Japanese were able to utilize the most advanced and modern fishing tools and methods, backed by political power. Our old-fashioned fishing industry was naturally unable to compete, and therefore, its decline and decay were inevitable.

The earliest Japanese fishing presence in Shandong Province was undoubtedly in Qingdao. We can say that Qingdao was the headquarters of Japanese fishing in Shandong. It is recorded that the Japanese came to Qingdao to fish starting in 1914, when they seized Qingdao from the Germans. At that time, due to various conveniences granted by our government, the number of Japanese fishing boats in Qingdao increased from 108 to more than 130 between 1915 and 1917, with the number of fishermen peaking in 1916, totaling 561. By 1918, the number of fishing boats had decreased to 93, and the number of fishermen had decreased to 440. According to a survey by the Japanese consulate in Qingdao in 1925, there were 49 resident fishermen and 309 fishing laborers. In 1928, according to a municipal survey, there were a total of 34 Japanese fishing boats, including 30 large sailing vessels and 4 small motorboats, with a total of 300 fishermen. According to recent surveys, there are 45 Japanese fishing boats in Qingdao, including 38 large sailing vessels and 7 diesel-powered vessels, with 500 fishermen. They reside in Qingdao year-round, engage in fishing, and have organized the Qingdao Aquatic Products Cooperative as their marketing agency. (Note 11)

It should also be noted here: why has the number of Japanese fishing boats decreased from 108 to 45? Does this indicate that Japanese fishing in Qingdao is gradually declining? Of course not! Because Japan's recent fishing operations in Shandong have Qingdao as the center between the Yellow Sea and the East China Sea, and Weihaiwei as the center between the Yellow Sea and the Bohai Sea. In the past, they focused solely on Qingdao, but now, in addition to Qingdao as a base, they are also developing towards the Weihaiwei area. Therefore, in Qingdao, they have inevitably had to slightly divert some of their fishing power; but this does not prove that Japanese fishing in Qingdao has declined. On the contrary, it precisely proves that Japanese fishing has developed from Qingdao to all fish-producing areas of Shandong.

The most commonly caught fish by the Japanese in Qingdao is Spanish mackerel. Spanish mackerel are caught using fly fishing. Every spring, the larger Japanese ships sail to the Spanish mackerel fishing grounds of Haizhou, while the smaller boats operate near Mount Shuiling and Dagong Island. In summer, the range is wider, and in autumn, they are mostly in the vicinity of Dalian Island and Thousand Li Island... It is estimated that each large ship catches about 7,000 yuan worth of fish annually, and even in lean years, they catch about 2,000 yuan worth. Besides Spanish mackerel, the next most common fish is swordfish, which is most abundant in Shazikou, Taixi Town. In 1915, 18 fishing boats came from Oita Prefecture in Japan, followed by 10 boats from Dalian. Since then, several boats have come and gone every year. If there are fewer Spanish mackerel in summer, they catch eel, and when the hairtail fish scatter in autumn, they catch Spanish mackerel. At the beginning of each fishing season, the Japanese use Dagong Island, Mount Shuiling, Shazikou, Rongshan... as fishing grounds. At the peak of the fishing season, the area near Thousand Li Island is the most prosperous; at the end of the fishing season, some also venture far to Laoshan Bay or south to Dalian Island. It is estimated that each boat catches about 700 to 1,300 yuan worth of fish annually. Sharks are very useful; their fins are dried to make shark fins, their bones can be used to make utensils, their meat can be salted and dried for food, their skin can be boiled into glue or made into meat wings, and their livers can be rendered into oil to make candles. Therefore, the Japanese make huge profits, totaling tens of thousands of yuan annually.

As for the capture of flounder and halibut, each boat can catch at least 500 yuan worth of fish in each fishing season; each boat can also catch about 500 yuan worth of sea bass in each fishing season. In addition, the Japanese also use diving equipment to catch abalone and sea cucumber, with each boat earning 1,800 yuan, and up to 2,000 yuan or more. According to a survey from 1932, the total amount of fish caught by the Japanese in Qingdao was 3,965,264 guan (each guan is equal to 100.5335 taels), valued at 1,955,708 yuan. (Note 12) Shandong has lost such good fishing rights. Can the future of its fishing industry still be asked about?

Note 10: See the Qingdao Municipal Social Affairs Bureau's report to the Ministry of Industry, published in the Shanghai Shenbao on November 24, 1934.

Note 12: Same as note 6.

Plans for Reforming Shandong's Fishing Industry

From the above sections, it can be seen that the output of Shandong's fishing industry is indeed remarkable. Although it has now reached a state of decline and decay, it is not too late to catch up and find ways to save it. In recent years, the Shandong Provincial Department of Construction, in order to rectify the coastal fishing industry in Shandong, has issued many measures for salvation, but most of them focus on treating the symptoms while neglecting the root cause. Therefore, the Department stated in its plan for rectifying the coastal fishing industry in Shandong: "...The fishing industry is now on the verge of bankruptcy. If we do not immediately seek to treat the symptoms to maintain the current situation, it will be even more difficult to save in the future..." So what are their methods? "...For the present, we can expand this place and change it into a Fisheries Protection Bureau, temporarily purchase two protection warships to prevent pirates, establish fish markets to avoid exploitation by fish merchants, and establish fishermen's loan offices to facilitate fishermen's turnover..."

These methods can be said to focus on treating the symptoms. In other words, they are effective ways to save Shandong's endangered fishing industry. However, this is not enough, because treating the symptoms is a temporary measure. If we do not address the root cause, treating the symptoms will lose its basis. Even if it can achieve considerable results, its effect will be minimal. Therefore, I advocate that treating the root cause and treating the symptoms should be carried out simultaneously. We should thoroughly reform Shandong's fishing industry from the root cause, and strive to maintain the current situation and implement salvation strategies from the perspective of treating the symptoms. Focusing solely on treating the root cause or solely emphasizing treating the symptoms are not perfect solutions.

Today, if we want to implement a plan to reform Shandong's fishing industry, we must first understand the reasons for the decline of Shandong's fishing industry. Only by implementing methods to address both the root cause and the symptoms can we achieve both goals. The reasons for the decline of Shandong's fishing industry can be summarized as follows:

Squeezed out by Japanese fisheries. The Japanese have recently used Dalian as a fishing base and used modern fishing nets to frequently cross the border to fish in the coastal areas of Shandong. Every fishing season, they come in groups. Shandong fishermen, due to the disparity in strength, retreat one after another, so the good fishing opportunities are seized by others.

Looting by bandits. In recent years, the rural economy in Shandong has been devastated, and many unemployed fishermen have gathered into gangs, appearing and disappearing unpredictably. They are nominally fishing, but in reality, they specialize in looting wealth and stealing nets, and even sinking people into the sea and sailing away, or threatening fishermen to pay a certain amount of money every year.

Exploitation by fish merchants. In the coastal ports of Shandong, except for Qingdao, which has a commercially-run fish market, the rest are managed by fish merchants who monopolize fish prices, manipulate the market, deduct commissions, and practice high-interest exploitation. Fishermen feel great pain and can do nothing about it, causing the fishing economy to be extremely panicked.

Conservative and outdated methods, unaware of improvement. Shandong fishermen, due to economic difficulties, ignorance, and lack of ability to improve, use fishing gear and methods that have been inherited for many years. Competing with foreigners is undoubtedly a failure. Therefore, fishermen's livelihoods are becoming increasingly difficult, and imported marine products are becoming increasingly large. Except for a few Jianglun boats that can still support themselves, more and more poor fishermen are changing their professions to make a living. This has further pushed Shandong's fishing industry to the brink of bankruptcy.

I believe that strengthening ourselves is the best creed for reforming Shandong's fishing industry today. The reasons for the decline of Shandong's fishing industry over the years should be considered from the perspective of our own reform, rather than attributing it to external pressure and dumping of foreign goods. To reform Shandong's fishing industry, we should start with the following aspects:

Establish a Fisheries Protection Bureau. The establishment of this bureau is dedicated to managing the administrative affairs of the fishing industry in the entire province, leading all technical matters, developing aquatic products, improving manufacturing, and protecting the safety of fishermen. Fishing is a major economic source in Shandong, and there should be a specialized agency to design and manage it. If it is still under the jurisdiction of the Department of Construction, there will often be problems of insufficient attention to affairs. Over the years, Shandong's fishing industry, with the exception of Qingdao, has mostly lacked a specialized agency to manage it. Everything is left to its own devices. External aggression has not been negotiated, and internal organization lacks a high-level agency to supervise and improve it. Therefore, the establishment of a Fisheries Protection Bureau is necessary at present.

Establish a Fisheries Police Force. This is specifically designed to defend against pirates and unreasonable aggression by foreign fishing boats. Roughly, the fishing grounds along the coast of Shandong should be permanently stationed with police forces to provide defense, so that fishermen can be protected and not suffer more external losses. The management of this police force should preferably be directly subordinate to the jurisdiction of the Fisheries Protection Bureau, so as to facilitate direct command.

Build fishing ports. Because fishing ports have a close relationship with the fishing industry, fishing ports are the base of the fishing industry. They not only provide many conveniences for the transportation, sale, processing, and storage of fish catches, but also are necessary for the construction, mooring, and repair of fishing boats, the production and repair of fishing gear, the avoidance of wind disasters, and the supply of various necessities for fishing operations. (To be continued)

Chunqiu (Annals)

Birds Naming Themselves 205

— (Zhezun)

There are poems from the Tang Dynasty about mountain birds naming themselves. Paying close attention, it is indeed not a mistake. For example, magpies and sparrows, their calls seem to carry the sound of the word "magpie"; the crow's call seems to carry the sound of the word "crow"; the myna's call seems to carry the sound of the word "myna." As for other birds, such as the cuckoo, which calls "Cut wheat, plant rice, better to return," they are all calling out their own names, blurting them out. I believe that birds are inherently ignorant and simply produce natural sounds. How could they understand how to call themselves by name? An ancient person also wrote a line, "A forest of bird language misses divination with poetry." My humble opinion is that the various birds must have existed first, and when Cangjie created the characters, he listened to the calls of the various birds, copied and depicted them, and then determined their names. Therefore, the names could match the reality. Mencius said, "In the time of Yao, the flood raged, and the paths of beasts and birds crossed in China." This shows that when humans first came into being, birds and animals were also produced at the same time. Therefore, Cangjie's creation of characters was also based on pre-existing things, and then a combination of indication and pictography was made.

Father's Pigeons 206

— Yi Zhen

Recently, my father bought two pigeons from somewhere. These pigeons have feathers as white as rice flour, and a pair of blood-red eyes, as if inlaid with a pair of rubies. They are very beautiful and intelligent, and their parents have given them a pair of strong wings, which further enhances their health and beauty.

On the first day, they recognized their home, food trough, water basin, and their loving owner.

Every day when my father returned from the office, he would lean against the window and silently watch the pair of things. Sometimes, he would sprinkle a handful of grains in the food trough, and the always content pigeons would always fly over "dodo dodo," whether standing on the wall or on the roof. My father named them "Abai." "Abai" was very obedient and often flew to stand in front of my father. But when my father raised his hand to stroke their adorable white feathers, they would "flap flap flap" and fly away.

"Abai" was very good at acting cute, so my father loved them even more.

This time, my father went to Beijing for business, and the pigeons were entrusted to me. I was very worried that they would run away one day. In his first letter, he asked about the family and also specifically mentioned Abai's living conditions. My father also said that if Abai were not too young, he would take them as long-term travel companions. Perhaps this letter could be brought by Abai, which would be even more secure and faster than registered mail.

My father's treatment of Abai can be said to be meticulous. I wonder if Abai's heart has retained my father's impression?

Duck 207

— Jiaoxin

Ducks were called "wu" in ancient times; those smaller than ducks are called "fu," and "fu" are wild ducks.

Nanjing's "pressed duck" is famous, but in fact, Nanjing's production is not very large, and most of it comes from the Qinghuai area north of the Yangtze River. It is said that the annual sales of ducks are over 40 million, and at 8 jiao per duck, the annual cost is 32 million yuan. This figure is quite alarming. Some people say that if the money spent on eating ducks were used to buy airplanes, 320 airplanes could be bought, which would have some effect on national defense. This is certainly true, but on the other hand, what about the people who rely on it for a living?

According to traditional Chinese medicine, ducks are extremely cold in nature and are the mother of malaria, so those suffering from "gentleman's disease" (a euphemism for malaria) should never eat them.

In Qidong County, Jiangsu, when inviting guests, it is customary to offer the duck's head to the guest of honor. When asked why, they are also mystified, but it is simply a custom that has been passed down.

There are two small glands in the duck's anus that are said to have the fragrance of pine nuts, so many people like to eat them, but I have never dared to try them.

God's Spoiled Children 208

When the revolutionary army first came, women rushed to cut their hair. At that time, women who cut their hair were called "duck's butt." This is very similar in shape! (Nanjing constructs "two-way fur," but I don't know where the meaning comes from.)

Although ducks are not often seen in poetry, the memorable one is "Spring river water warms, ducks know first." As for the two words "duck stove," they are often seen, because ancient incense burners were duck-shaped, so the word "duck" was used in conjunction.

Ducks are fat and bloated, and they waddle when they walk, with a great deal of gentlemanly demeanor.

Wild Duck 209

— Xiafei

Wild ducks, also known as "jiu" or "water ducks," are said to be nourishing to yin. Therefore, in winter, those who live near Taihu Lake mostly rely on catching wild ducks for a living. Because wild ducks are a delicacy in their hometown, in winter, almost every high-end wine and dinner banquet will have one such dish; and some people also give ducks with their feathers as gifts to relatives and friends. As for the price, it is about half a yuan per jin. Although this number does not seem very expensive to us, it is really considered unusual in a poor and remote rural area with a very low standard of living. Now I will write down the methods of catching and cooking them:

Catching: Wild ducks are good at flying, so catching them is not easy, but in my hometown, I know three kinds: Firing with a shotgun. But this method is not used by many, because once lead bullets are left in the wild duck's meat, the flavor will lose its freshness, and you have to be careful not to damage your teeth with the lead bullets when eating. Catching with a net. However, this method is very troublesome; you must first catch a small wild duck and raise it together with your own domestic duck. When it grows up, cut off the tips of its wing feathers so that it can fly but not soar. In this way, with some training, you can then spread a net on the lake, put some grains in the net's area, and put the "duck decoy" in the middle to let it jump freely. When a flock of wild ducks flies past, it will also fly around the edge of the net, so some wild ducks will often be lured into the net. At that time, the catcher, who is lurking in the reed mat, can close the net door, turning many active wild ducks into prisoners in his net. It is to use "fairy traps"; they are a few bamboo strips and a ramie rope. They arrange ten or twenty bamboo bows with a spring mechanism in the reed mat overnight, put some food on the spring mechanism, and go to retrieve them early the next morning. Then one or two pairs of wild ducks will be caught in these dozens of fairy traps.

Cooking: If you want to eat wild duck, you should know about the cooking of wild duck; because wild ducks are not like domestic ducks, they often live in water and eat fish and shrimp, so they have a very heavy fishy smell, especially when plucking feathers. - Wild duck feathers should be plucked dry and not moistened. The soft feathers and blood vessel feathers should be plucked clean, and no feather stubs should be left behind. Then you can put them in water to open the belly. However, there are also two ways to cook them, but it depends on the personality and preferences of the person eating them: Stir-fry with shepherd's purse, with shredded meat or pure duck. Buy half a jin of pork and stuff it in a duck's belly, then stew it in a wok over charcoal fire, but you need to put more wine. It's best to eat it while it's hot. Not only does reheating taste inferior, but the fishy smell is unbearable.

Four-Winged Chicken 210

— (Ziwei)

Chickens are domestic fowl, with two wings and two feet. Everyone knows this, but it is strange to have a chicken with four wings.

Yesterday, I visited the Guanshengyuan Farm in Caohejing. After admiring the brocade carp and red maples, I encountered a chicken coop. In the middle was a rooster with plump, brocade feathers. At first glance, it was no different from ordinary chickens, but upon closer inspection, there were long hairs like brooms between its feet, and two wings were growing between them. They were displayed all day long, just like a fan, yellow in color, and slightly smaller than the original two wings. Is this a deformed development among chickens?

According to Mr. Someone, a receptionist at the farm, this chicken was given as a special gift by Mr. Shen, the director of the Yuhang Pasture of the Hangzhou West Lake Milk Company. Since the arrival of the four-winged chicken at the park, people from far and wide have flocked to see it, and everyone praised it for its uniqueness.

Little Western Paradise 211

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 22: Heroic Words Move Painted Lips, Beautiful Women Gather to Discuss; False Affection Startles Jade Wrists, Suffering Woman Flees Imprisonment

This sudden turn of events captivated Bei Hai, making him unable to resist following them to see what would happen. He quickly ran to the front hall, sat down at the table where newspapers were kept, and while pretending to flip through the newspapers, he kept his eyes fixed on the window of that room. He saw Mrs. Zhou and Mrs. Liu both leaning sideways, sitting by the window, while Jia Duocai was sitting on the bed, his face turned slightly away from the window. Just by looking at the two deep wrinkles slanting down his cheeks, one could tell that he was extremely displeased, constantly displaying a forced smile to his guests. The young Mrs. Yueying was sitting there, but not visible. He only heard Mrs. Liu say, "Of course, you both are willing. But the woman's willingness is just a facade, isn't it?" Jia Duocai laughed, "It's good that you all can say that. Anyway, I'm not forcing her to marry me." Mrs. Liu's shrill voice rose a little higher as she said, "Although you're not forcing her to marry you, you've treated her like a prisoner since she married you. Even her grandmother, who longs to see her granddaughter and is near death, you don't let her out to meet her. This is only the beginning of her being in your house, and you're already treating her like this. In the future, when you take her away from this place, won't you devour her alive? So, for the sake of humanity, we can't help but stand up and save her life." Jia Duocai laughed, "You're exaggerating. I have no grudge against Miss Zhu, why would I want her life?" Mrs. Liu said, "If you continue like this, it's worse than killing her with a knife. You're simply cutting her flesh bit by bit." Just then, a sobbing sound was heard, as someone cried out. But the crying didn't last long and stopped immediately. Mrs. Zhou said, "Don't cry. Now that we're here talking to you, we'll definitely come up with a solution." Mrs. Liu said, "Mr. Jia, you see, she can't help but cry when we get to this point. This is definitely not something she can fake. She's only with you because she has no other choice. If you keep her locked up, she'll suffocate to death." Jia Duocai didn't say anything, but sat there with a sullen face. (381)

Miscellaneous Talk

On Peacocks 212

— By the Master of the Paper Curtain and Bronze Vase Studio

Among feathered creatures, few are as outstanding as the peacock. Its form is somewhat like a pheasant, with a body length of over three feet and short, small wings. The male is particularly magnificent, with long tail feathers adorned with golden and emerald green patterns in the shape of eyes, arranged on the upper part, extremely dazzling. It is native to tropical regions, and those raised in our country's gardens are mostly imported from the Indian archipelago and Siam.

The introduction of peacocks into our country dates back very early. The "Yi Zhou Shu" says, "People from afar present peacock birds." In ancient times, it was mentioned alongside geese and kingfishers. The "Tai Xuan Jing" says, "The etiquette of peacocks and geese can be emulated," with a note saying, "Geese fly in formation, and peacocks also form lines." The "Comprehensive Mirror" says, "In the first year of Zhongxing during the reign of Emperor He of Qi, gold and silver were used to make armor, decorated with peacock and kingfisher feathers," with a note saying, "peacock and kingfisher feathers." There is also a saying that peacocks mate with snakes, as the "Nan Yue Zhi" says, "Peacocks do not necessarily pair up for mating, they can conceive simply by connecting through sound and shadow, similar to mating with snakes." "Mao Ting Ke Hua" says, "Snakes mate with peacocks, and some obtain their eggs. If a chicken incubates them, they hatch, and the offspring is called 'Duhu'."

Regarding the method of catching peacocks, it is said that "Peacocks take great pleasure in their tails. Whenever they want to perch on a mountain, they must first choose a place to put their tails, and then stop. Those who catch them often wait for heavy rain, when the tail becomes heavy with rain and cannot fly high. Even if people arrive, the peacock loves its tail and fears it will be injured, so it no longer flies. The catcher can then capture it."

The phrase "chosen from the peacock screen" refers to this bird acting as a matchmaker. However, there are also instances of the same species acting as matchmakers. The "Bei Hu Lu" says, "Tame peacocks are used to lure wild peacocks, called 'peacock matchmakers'."

Peacocks enjoy dancing, no less than modern fashionable women. "Ji Wen" says, "When peacocks hear the sounds of pipes and songs, they must stretch their wings and tails, glancing around and dancing." "Hua Duan" says, "The Kingdom of Silla presented dancing peacocks. Emperor Dezong summoned Bian Guang at Zhenwu Gate to paint their portraits." "Yi Wu Zhi" says, "Peacocks dance when people clap their hands." "Jin Gong Qing Zan" says, "During the reign of Emperor Shizu, the Western Regions presented peacocks that could understand human speech and dance to the beat of finger-snapping." Li Fang's poem says, "Peacocks dance in pairs to welcome the sun."

There are many different names for peacocks, such as Zhong Hui's "Ode to the Peacock," which says, "There is a magnificent bird from the fiery region." "Ben Cao" says, "The peacock is also called Yue Wu." Shi Zhen said, "Kong means 'large'." In Sanskrit, it is called Mayura. "Tan Yuan" says, "Li Xun kept five birds, and called the peacock 'Southern Guest'."

"Mi Zang Ji" says, "The Peacock King Mother Bodhisattva holds an open lotus in her left hand and a peacock tail in her right." This is because peacocks have long been known as having nine virtues, which Buddhism uses to symbolize the conduct of monks.

Recently, I saw in the lost book "Hua Jian" that "Emperor Huizong ordered scholars to paint peacocks ascending a pier as screen decorations, but was greatly displeased. He then ordered the remaining sons to submit their best work, but even those who put in their utmost effort were not used. They then pointed to the emperor and pleaded, and the emperor's decree said, 'Whenever a peacock ascends a pier, it must first use its left foot. All of your paintings show it using its right foot first.' Upon verification, this was indeed the case, and all were convinced by the emperor's exquisite understanding of things."

Peacocks spread their wings when they see people wearing beautiful clothes, which is commonly called "opening the screen." I once visited Hanbi Villa in Wumen. Peacocks were kept in a large cage. When a beautifully dressed young woman gracefully walked past them, the peacocks seemed unwilling to hide their beauty, and spread their magnificent feathers, their intricate patterns shimmering, resembling the changing colors of clouds and mist, which was admired as a spectacle.

During the Qing Dynasty, peacock feathers were used as decorations on the back of official hats, similar to the ancient practice of wearing sable tails. Initially, this was done to reward meritorious service, and only those who had made significant contributions and received special favor were granted the honor of wearing them. After the Xianfeng era, the practice became abused, and a system of purchasing peacock feathers was established. As a result, officials of the fifth rank and above could purchase them, and they were no longer highly valued. However, the wearing of double-eyed peacock feathers by senior officials was still a sign of special favor. Triple-eyed peacock feathers could only be worn by princes and beiles, and were considered as valuable as a bestowed yellow riding jacket. A previous poem says, "The hat flutters with peacock feathers in the gentle breeze, the goose-yellow robe is imbued with imperial aura," referring to this.

There is a so-called peacock flower, likely named for its similar shape. The "Nan Yue Bi Ji" says, "In Qiongzhou, there is a peacock flower," and a poem about the summer heat says, "The linen garment is half-untied as sweat flows, freezing to death the peacock flower in the shade of the wall." The flower thrives in shade and dampness, and brings a chill when facing it, hence the saying. There is also a so-called malachite, which is bright green and shiny, with those whose patterns resemble peacock tails being considered most valuable, used as decorations for hairpins and bracelets. The powdered form can be used for eye treatments.

"Peacocks have gold and emerald feathers, which grow in early spring and wither after March or April, withering and flourishing together with the calyx." This is seen in "Pi Ya." "Peacock feathers stick together when dragon brain is applied, as things of the same kind are attracted to each other," seen in "Qun Zhuang Man Lu." "Peacocks chirp in harmony to greet the morning," seen in "Yi Wu Zhi." "The Yunnan region produces peacocks, which often fly in pairs and leave after more than a month," seen in "Hua Yang Guo Zhi." All of the above statements have not been mentioned by modern zoologists and can be used for research.

Ancient people often praised peacocks with famous lines, such as Han Yu's, "Emerald horns stand tall and uniquely, golden flowers shimmer in contrast." Pi Rixiu says, "Forcibly listening to purple birds, they often want to dance, sleepily leaning on red trees, resembling relying on a screen." Li Ying says, "A body of gold and emerald cannot be painted, few come from ten thousand mountains and rivers." Xue Neng says, "Once lived in the mountains, truly hidden by mist, every time passing under the court, resembling the arrival of spring," all of which are worth reciting.
